The Mongolian Political Committee Telegrams Request for Increased Funding 15

(Beijing) Guihua telegram: The two Princes Yun and Sha, in the name of the Chairman and Vice-Chairman of the Mongolian Political Committee, telegraphed the central government on the 21st, requesting increased funding and construction funds, stating that the Mongolian Political Committee is temporarily using the temple site for office, but now that the lease has expired, the monks are urging them to leave, and they have moved to the wilderness for tent office on the 13th. In a blink of an eye, it will be a harsh winter, how can they maintain it? Therefore, building the office site is an urgent need at present. The original budget has been reduced as much as possible. If it is approved as it is, it is still feared that it will not be enough. Now it is set at 20,000, which is not enough to cope. Please consider the difficulties of Mongolia and approve it according to the original amount. (22nd Special Dispatch)

British Representative Arrives in Guangdong to Negotiate the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway Treaty Revision; Advocates Holding Meeting in Hong Kong; Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce Opposes Track Connection 22

(Hong Kong) The Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce telegraphed on the 21st, opposing the track connection between the Guangzhou-Kowloon and Guangdong-Hankou railways, stating that the predecessors established the terminal station in Dashatou, clearly indicating that there would be no room for track connection. Because after the track connection, it would hinder the progress of Guangzhou's commerce. (22nd Special Dispatch)

Headquarters Issues Circular to All Provinces: Six-Year Opium Prohibition 23

(Nanchang) Public announcement: The Headquarters recently issued a circular to the provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, etc., stating that opium has been strictly prohibited since the Qing Dynasty, but planting, transportation, sale, and smoking are still prevalent everywhere. Furthermore, red pills, golden elixir, morphine, and heroin have emerged as replacements. All laws and regulations have become mere paperwork, and the malpractices are endless. Therefore, the National Assembly's six-year prohibition plan is adopted. All aspects of planting, transportation, sale, and smoking will be strictly managed and controlled, and then gradually eliminated.

The following measures will be implemented: (1) Prohibit smoking, starting with the party, government, military, and academic circles. Ordinary people will be treated in hospitals for addiction. Those who cannot quit in a short period will gradually reduce their dosage and quit within six years. (2) Soil paste shops are only allowed to reduce, not increase. (3) The interior will first eliminate tobacco planting. Provinces in remote areas that have not planted tobacco are not allowed to plant. Those who cannot plant food crops must report the acreage and reduce it gradually by area each year. (4) Monitor the quantity of supply and demand, and implement unified collection and transportation to prevent smuggling. In addition, the following three points are emphasized: (1) Soil paste shops are not allowed to turn on lights. (2) Smoking licenses are not allowed to be lent to others or to open opium dens. (3) No gentry or officials are allowed to monopolize. The regulations for prohibiting smoking households, investigating and banning narcotic drugs, prohibiting soil paste shops, strictly prohibiting the planting of tobacco, and prohibiting the purchase of soil from distant production areas will also be issued. (22nd Special Dispatch)

After the Xiamen-Taiwanese Gambling Den Was Raided, Two Incidents of Bomb Discovery; Public Security Bureau Temporarily Imposes Martial Law; Certain Foreigners Armed Parade 24

(Xiamen) On the 20th, the Public Security Bureau's Detective Team raided the Taiwanese gambling den Qingfa Foreign Firm in Dashengli. The Japanese consulate intervened without a resolution. On the evening of the 21st, Chen Qingmu, the leader of the Second Detective Team, who set up Siyichun, was attacked with a bomb, which did not explode. On the afternoon of the 22nd, dozens of people came to demonstrate, but there was no conflict. At approximately 8:00 PM, in front of the Taiwanese Southeast Hotel on Siming North Road, a bomb suddenly exploded, injuring one rickshaw puller and one woman. The Public Security Bureau temporarily announced martial law. The source of the bomb is unknown. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Xiamen) After the bomb exploded at the Dongmen Hotel on the night of the 22nd, certain foreigners divided into five or six teams, each with twenty to thirty people, each holding submachine guns and pistols, parading along Siming Road, South Road, and Zhongshan Road. All night markets on the roads closed their doors. Japanese police went to the Southeast Hotel for inspection. The Public Security Bureau imposed martial law on all main roads. As of midnight, there were no changes. However, the source of the bomb is still unknown. (22nd Special Dispatch)

US Considering Extending Naval Conference for Five Years; World is Turbulent, Holding Meeting Next Year Will Be Fruitless; Hirota Prepares to Meet with British and American Ambassadors 57

(Washington) The Associated Press obtained reliable news today that the extension of the naval disarmament conference scheduled to be held next year to 1940 is now under serious consideration. The world is now turbulent, especially the Far East. It will be difficult to achieve any success if a meeting is held next year. Some diplomatic and naval circles are discussing the proposal to extend the reduction of naval armaments for five years. Hopes were originally slim, but recent events have completely extinguished even the slightest of hope. According to London sources, Britain also intends to expand its navy, so the future of the conference is extremely pessimistic. Some quarters suggest that delaying the meeting is the best way to postpone the final decision on naval policy for various countries. Countries can find ways to achieve mutual political understanding before 1940. For precautionary reasons, the United States can also expand its navy to the limits allowed by the London Treaty. By the end of 1936, the United States will be only 85 warships short of the treaty limit. After the conference is postponed, the 5:5:3 ratio stipulated by the London Treaty should still be maintained, and the Japanese proposal to increase the ratio can also be avoided. (21st National Telegram)

(Tokyo) Japan's policy for the naval disarmament conference next year is to participate on the premise that it is not restricted by the Washington and London treaties and that political issues are not discussed. However, it is recently rumored that British and American officials oppose Japan's demand to abolish the ratio agreement. If so, it will be difficult for Japan to implement its demands. Foreign Minister Hirota believes that if Britain and the United States deny Japan's demands on fundamental issues, the meeting next year may either break down or lead to Japan's withdrawal. Therefore, he is paying close attention to the true intentions of Britain and the United States. Depending on the situation, the Foreign Minister himself may personally hold preparatory meetings with the British and American ambassadors to explain Japan's demands, as the Foreign Minister has expressed his intention to take active action. (22nd Telecommunication Dispatch)

Japan Opposes Postponement of Naval Conference; Hirota Reports Progress to Cabinet 58

(Tokyo) There is now an opinion in the United States that since the next naval conference has no hope of success, there is no need to convene it and it would be better to postpone it. The US representatives in London also revealed the above informal opinion on the 21st. However, Ambassadors Saito in the United States and Matsudaira in the United Kingdom have not yet issued official telegrams to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs regarding this situation. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs believes that there is no reason to postpone the meeting next year. For the sake of the smooth development of the next conference, it has already participated in the preparatory negotiations. Unexpectedly, such remarks have been made, which is unexpected. Moreover, today, when no concrete proposals have been discovered in the preparatory negotiations, it is unbelievable that an authoritative delegation is releasing an atmosphere that the formal meeting cannot be established. However, according to the current treaty, by 1935, Japan will be able to maintain a considerable ratio compared to the United Kingdom and the United States. However, by 1936, the proportion of old battleships and other circumstances will be lower than 60%. If we still follow the current treaty, it will naturally be difficult to succumb. Under this reality, the conference in 1935 must be convened, and it is a natural policy to demand the correction of the current ratio. (22nd Japan Federation Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Just as the London disarmament preparatory conference was beginning to show signs of progress, a section of the US political world, citing the chaotic political situation in the Far East, advocated postponing the disarmament conference until 1940. This opinion is quite noteworthy. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs' intention regarding this is as follows: The reason why Plenipotentiary Wakatsuki signed at the London disarmament conference was that the London Treaty was a temporary agreement until 1936, which only had temporary effect. Moreover, the contracting countries are stipulated that they can participate in the disarmament conference in 1935 with a free position. Therefore, postponing the conference can be said to be a violation of the spirit of the Washington and London treaties. The reason for the US's hope to postpone it is that by 1940, the warship construction plan will be fully completed, and it will possess the actual power of the world's number one and will use this to suppress the demands of the UK, Japan, etc. However, this self-centered attitude is detrimental to the success of the conference and the preservation of peace in the Far East. It lies in the fact that the UK and the US recognize the political self in the Far East, and that it can be separated from the naval issue. Although the disarmament conference is postponed, if the US adopts an attitude of putting Japan's Far East issue on the scale with disarmament, it is feared that it will be difficult for the agreement to be established. Therefore, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs does not pay attention to the postponement of the disarmament conference. At the same time, the Navy also believes that this is a self-serving argument and dismisses it with a laugh. (22nd Telecommunication Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Today's routine cabinet meeting was held at the Prime Minister's official residence at 10:00 AM. Prime Minister Saito and other cabinet members attended. Foreign Minister Hirota reported the progress of the disarmament preparatory negotiations as follows: (1) The United Kingdom hopes to hold the meeting before the Emperor's celebration ceremony, advocating holding the meeting within January. The United States hopes to hold it in the summer due to parliamentary relations. Japan advocates holding it in April, so the date has not yet been decided. (2) The United Kingdom and the United States do not seem to oppose Japan's demand not to discuss the Far East issue. (3) As for the location of the meeting, the United Kingdom and the United States each advocate holding it in their own capitals, so it has not been decided. (4) As for the countries participating in the negotiations, Japan advocates the participation of the United Kingdom, Japan, the United States, France, and Italy. However, due to European relations, the participation of Germany, Russia, and Spain may be a problem. (22nd Telecommunication Dispatch)

All Parties Quietly Observe Developments 59

(London) As far as is generally known, in this morning's meeting between British and American naval experts, the British representatives submitted a list to the American representatives of the minimum number of warships and equipment required for British national defense, and explained the various technical and military reasons. The American delegation will send this document to the Navy Department in Washington, and further negotiations will continue after the government expresses its opinion. The United States has not submitted a document of the same nature, and is still adopting a wait-and-see attitude. So far, it has only filed the outline explained by the British representatives regarding British naval policy. The document submitted by the British experts this morning is temporary in nature, and its contents can be referred to and revised with reference to the naval policies of other countries. It is said that the British naval organization will undergo changes after the expiry of the Washington and London naval treaties. Whether the two naval treaties will be extended or revised after their expiry is the purpose of the 1935 naval conference. (21st Havas Dispatch)

(Tokyo) According to the report of Ambassador Matsudaira stationed in the United Kingdom, the British policy for the naval conference preparatory negotiations is not to decide on procedures in a hurry, but to freely exchange opinions with Japan and the United States, and resolve them after Prime Minister MacDonald consults with the representatives of the two countries at an appropriate time. Therefore, the venue and time of the formal meeting, the topics of discussion, etc., can be decided after France and Italy participate. (22nd Japan Federation Dispatch)

(Rome) Il Lavoro, the organ of the Fascist Party, commented on the 1935 naval conference, saying that if Germany and Russia participate at the same time as the United Kingdom, the United States, Japan, France, and Italy, and become a seven-nation conference, it will have great political value. Such a conference may appear on the surface to be holding technical negotiations, but in reality, it is seeking compromises among countries in order to achieve a balance of power with each other. (21st Havas Dispatch)

Britain Advocates Expanding Navy 60

(London) Among the British newspapers, the Labour Party's organ, the Daily Herald, publishes the most news about the preparatory negotiations for the 1935 naval conference. The reason is that the Conservative Party has repeatedly stated that the current state of the British Navy is dangerous, and the government will inevitably use the opportunity of this preparatory negotiation to satisfy the Conservative Party. The Labour Party's organ is well aware of this. Its claim is that on the one hand, it wants to reduce land armaments, and on the other hand, it should not reorganize sea armaments. However, the policy adopted by the British government for the next naval conference is not a policy of reducing armaments, but a policy of large-scale reorganization of armaments. The contents of the document submitted by Naval Minister Monsell to the American experts at the meeting of British and American experts yesterday morning are astonishing. The document stated that, from a technical perspective of imperial national defense and the security of imperial trade routes, the United Kingdom must require the following: (1) After the expiration of the Washington Naval Treaty, the United Kingdom should build a new main fleet. (2) Build 30 new cruisers to increase the number of cruisers to 70, because 10 of the original 50 cruisers will be old and unusable in two years, so they can only be used as 40. (3) Build many destroyers. (4) Build many aircraft carriers. The Daily Herald therefore believes that the 1927 naval conference failed due to British policy, and now Britain has returned to its policy at that time. In short, this request by the United Kingdom will inevitably cause an unpleasant reaction from the United States, because even if the United States allows the United Kingdom's request, the Japanese Navy will inevitably demand the same increase, which the United States cannot allow. The Daily Herald editorial also stated that those who advocate a strong naval policy have repeatedly forced the government to follow their claims and repeatedly urged continental countries to reduce or limit their naval armaments. However, is it not strange that what our government opposes is only the reorganization of armaments on land, while it is resolutely proceeding with the reorganization of armaments at sea? (22nd Havas Dispatch)

Taiwan to Excavate Mountains to Facilitate Military Traffic 61

Taipei The Taiwan Army believes that in times of war, both sides of Taiwan Island will be attacked by the enemy. However, the east and west coasts are separated by a high mountain, called the Central Mountain Range, which makes transportation very inconvenient. It has sent technicians to investigate excavation methods. According to its report, the Taiwan Army believes that it is easier to excavate and has decided to start work soon, which is expected to be completed within two years. (22nd China United Telegram)

Soviet Russia Unifies Military Power: Supreme Military Organs Reorganized, Foreign Policy Advances Bravely Along a Peaceful Path 62

(Moscow) A decree from the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union orders the abolition of the core staff of the Revolutionary Military Council of the Soviet Union and the People's Commissariat of the Army and Navy. The Army and Navy Commissariat is renamed the Soviet Defense Commissariat, and Gamarnik and Tukhachevsky are appointed as assistants to the People's Commissar of Defense. (TASS dispatch, 20th)

(Moscow) An editorial in the Soviet government gazette, Izvestia, states: "The renaming of the Army and Navy Commissariat as the Defense Commissariat is intended to emphasize the fact that the purpose of the entire Soviet military system is defense, with absolutely no intention of aggression, attack, or military expansion. The Soviet Army and Navy, by their very nature, cannot be used as weapons of aggression. The renaming of the Army Commissariat itself further reinforces this concept." The newspaper continues, "The Soviet government is implementing its clear and concrete peace plan in all aspects and along all avenues of its activities. This peace policy is not a chance detour but the essence of proletarian diplomacy. Currently, the Soviet government is relying on its diplomatic organs to pursue it bravely and resolutely. At the same time, this policy is supported by the working masses of both the Soviet Union and capitalist countries, and the Soviet Army and Navy (defenders of peace and their socialist homeland) are developing and strengthening under this banner of peace." (TASS dispatch, 21st)

Current Affairs Commentary

Further Discussion on Rescuing the Fishing Industry 63

— Jie Fang

The importance of the fishing industry is now universally recognized. This newspaper recently discussed the lack of vitality in our country's fishing industry and the ways to rescue it. Feeling that the ideas were not fully expressed, I present them again to serve as a supplement.

In recent times, the hardship of our country's aquatic products industry has reached its extreme. Speaking of fishing, there are pirates and the encroachment of strong neighbors, and fishing villages are showing signs of bankruptcy. Speaking of sales, fish prices are low, the market is chaotic, and fishermen lack financial regulation. If this continues, the complete collapse of the fishing industry is inevitable. Although there are thousands of reasons for this, the root cause lies in three external factors:

First, the knowledge of those engaged in fishing is limited and outdated. Fishermen cannot explore distant fishing grounds and only know how to compete for catches in coastal areas. Although they know that catches are decreasing year by year, they remain passive and unchanging. Fish merchants always concentrate the distribution of fish products in one place and do not know how to distribute products to different locations. They are also trapped by the exploitation of fish markets. Although fish prices plummet and profits are meager, fish products are still imported as usual. Fish markets do not improve their routine systems at all and only seek their own immediate interests, without considering the interests of fishermen and merchants. They do not know that the relationship between fishermen, fish merchants, and fish markets is very close, like lips and teeth. If fishermen and fish merchants are eliminated, how can the fish markets survive alone?

The second is the dumping of imported aquatic products. Since China opened its ports, aquatic product trade has always been in deficit. In recent years, various countries have developed their aquatic product industries, and facing domestic economic panic, they all seek an outlet, regarding China's market as their dumping ground. Japan is particularly prominent in this regard, with annual leakages reaching tens of thousands of dollars.

Third, the encroachment of Japanese fishing vessels. In recent years, Japan has actively developed its deep-sea fishing industry and has even greater ambitions for maritime rights in our country. Therefore, our country's coast is full of Japanese fishing boats that indiscriminately fish. The fish they catch are sold at reduced prices in various ports along our coast to sell them quickly and continue fishing. As a result, the fish that our fishermen work hard to catch must also be sold at low prices. The impact is such that many cannot maintain their livelihoods. It is no wonder that our country's aquatic products industry has been declining year by year.

All three of these factors are the driving forces behind the collapse of our country's fishing industry. If we want to urgently seek rescue, we must pay attention to the following strategies:

First, we must urgently stabilize fishing villages. Fishing villages are the foundation of the fishing industry. If fishing villages are safe, fishermen can live and work in peace. If fishermen live and work in peace, they can calmly plan the development of the fishing industry. Today, the bankruptcy of fishing villages and the rampant piracy are mutually reinforcing. The arrival of pirates is due to the decreasing fish production and the difficulty of fishermen's livelihoods, as well as the exploitation by local bullies and the extortion by government officials. Fishermen are under heavy pressure and cannot bear the suffering. The strong often become bandits. Once they become pirates, they turn to disturb the people. This cycle continues endlessly, which is why fishing villages are not peaceful. The way to stabilize fishing villages lies in maintaining law and order and guiding fishing. The implementation can start by delineating fishing areas and sending people who are familiar with maritime conditions and have aquatic knowledge to be responsible for guidance. If the whole country can advance simultaneously, the results will be faster. Second, we must improve fishing organizations. Those engaged in fishing in our country have a strong sense of association and form groups with feudal characteristics, such as the Fishermen's Guilds in the outer seas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. However, their work is only to resolve disputes among fishermen and request police protection in the name of the guild. In addition, they are indifferent to how to improve their own business, how to cooperate in production and sales, and how to prevent theft. The common facilities that modern social organizations should have are also lacking. Our country's Fishermen's Association Law has long been promulgated, but there are only three formal fishermen's associations in Shandong, fourteen in Jiangsu, six in Zhejiang, three in Fujian, and two in Anhui. The number is extremely limited. Even the work they advocate has not been fully realized. Therefore, fishermen in the outer seas still gather and disperse irregularly and cannot benefit from the organization. This is also something that needs to be improved urgently. Third, we must rationally distribute products. Our country's fish products are only concentrated in one place. Although the output has fallen drastically, the concentrated areas still feel that the supply exceeds demand, which leads to a drop in fish prices that cannot be reversed. The Ministry of Industry is actively preparing to establish a Shanghai fish market. It is said that the progress has reached a considerable level. Construction plans and organizational regulations are gradually taking shape, and it can officially open next spring. After this matter is realized, the distribution of fish products can be appropriately allocated according to the needs of various places. The Ministry of Railways is also working hard to add refrigerated vehicles. From now on, coastal fish products can be sold smoothly in the interior. With the expansion of sales channels, fish prices will naturally rise, and the lives of fishermen can also be slightly improved. However, these two things must be done carefully at the beginning, otherwise, they will only lose the trust of fishermen and fish merchants and will not help the actual situation.

Fourth, we must facilitate the circulation of aquatic product finance. Because our country's fish products are concentrated in one place, aquatic product finance is also controlled by the fish markets in one place. Fishermen's economic capital is mostly borrowed from fish markets, and there are various restrictions. Therefore, the establishment of a fishery bank is an urgent task. In the future, loan procedures can be handled by local fishermen's associations to make it easier to popularize among fishermen.

Fifth, we must popularize fishermen's education. Although our country's aquatic education has been carried out for a long time, it lacks the support of society and the promotion of the government. Moreover, the teaching staff often cannot provide students with knowledge that is relevant to the national conditions and profound academic knowledge. Generally, students lack the perseverance to be strong when they are in school, and after leaving school, they are ambitious and unwilling to work in the field. This is why the fishery education that has been promoted for more than 20 years has not achieved any success. Therefore, today, when we talk about aquatic education, we should change our original intentions. Mr. Niu Yongjian has strongly advocated fishermen's education. The public education center established in Songjiang County also has fishermen's education facilities. In the community education meeting of the sixth district of Jiangsu Province the day before yesterday, a proposal to pay attention to fishermen's education was also passed. This can be a model for various provinces and cities.

Sixth, we must revise the import tariff rates for aquatic products. Our country's fishing industry has been seriously harmed by the dumping of imported aquatic products. If we can give appropriate restrictions to imported goods, we can give the domestic products a chance to recover. However, before revising the tariff rules, we must have a deep understanding of the various imported goods before making a decision. Otherwise, if the tax rate is increased too much for those with fewer imports, and those who harm domestic products are not restricted, then it cannot be said to be a fair treatment.

In addition, the investigation of the national fishing industry, the promotion of fishing administration, and the prevention of Japanese fishing vessels from fishing have been discussed in detail in the previous commentary. I hope that those in power will pay attention to it.

Britain Intensifies Research on Aerial Tactics: Forms Special Unit for Special Training, New Single-Seat Aircraft to Be Publicly Exhibited 64

(London) It is reported that the British Air Force is now organizing a special unit to study aerial tactics, with pilots who were aerial combatants during the European War as assistants. Because the types of aircraft have greatly increased now, and after the failure of the Disarmament Conference, Britain will add several new air forces, special training is necessary. What will be tested to the best of its ability is the relative advantages and disadvantages of single-seat aircraft and two-seat aircraft. Single-seat aircraft fly faster and ascend more easily when soaring, but two-seat aircraft have stronger manpower and can combine bombing and combat. This special team will also study new tactics and new formations, and the possibility of placing more guns on aircraft, and the comparative advantages of biplanes. Three new single-seat aircraft secretly manufactured by the British Air Force will be displayed for the first time at the British Aircraft Exhibition on June 30. This new type of aircraft is powered by an air-cooled engine and has no water radiator. The weight of the fuselage is greatly reduced and it is not easily attacked by the enemy. The size of its speed is not yet known, but it is known that the red, white, and blue colors of the tail are no longer used because more paint will increase the weight of the aircraft. All protruding objects that may hinder the speed of the aircraft have been removed. (Reuters dispatch, 22nd)

Evening newspapers reported that the Little Entente had drafted two agreements and submitted them to French Foreign Minister Barthou. The first agreement advocates expanding the current Balkan Pact into an Eastern Locarno Pact, and the second agreement hopes to conclude a Mediterranean Pact including Soviet Russia and Italy. The French side seems to approve of this proposal and also proposes that Germany join the first pact and Italy join the second pact. A certain Tongjiu News Agency claimed that Barthou and Titulescu, representing France and the Little Entente, had reached an agreement with the following content: (1) Strictly abide by the Locarno Pact; (2) Conclude a Baltic Pact; (3) Conclude an Eastern Locarno Pact, including the Balkan countries, Soviet Russia, Czechoslovakia, Poland, and Germany; (4) Conclude a Mediterranean Pact, including Soviet Russia, the Little Entente countries, Bulgaria, Turkey, Italy, and France, with Italy and Poland as the main obstacles. Silencing the People's Mouth is a Great Loss: Criticizing the Maladministration of Germany 69

(Paris) German Deputy Prime Minister von Papen recently gave a speech at the University of Marburg, criticizing German domestic affairs, which caused a conflict with Propaganda Minister Goebbels. His speech was banned by the government and was never published. Recently, "Le Petit Parisien" obtained the main points of von Papen's speech and published them in the newspaper. Von Papen briefly said, "The task of the newspaper is to report the government's political mistakes, weaknesses, incompetence, and malpractices so that it can improve. This cannot be replaced by anonymous exposure and secret work organs. If this is used to measure it, then the German newspaper has lost its reason for existence. Who is without fault? The important thing is to listen to advice. Only the weak are unwilling to be criticized. One-party dictatorship is only a transitional political system. It should be abolished when the people can freely choose. I have never seen a country whose people can be clearly divided into two classes, one enjoying full rights and the other having their rights reduced. Perhaps only the system of Sparta is like this. Sparta divided the people into citizens and slaves, but the demise of Sparta was due to this. Is the German phenomenon going to restore the maladministration of Sparta? No amount of propaganda or organization can maintain the people's faith for a long time. For those who do not understand the authorities and criticize them, we can only humbly explain and persuade them, and should not incite young people to hate or threaten innocent people. Those who convince people with sincerity can make the people make considerable sacrifices for the country. If the people's mouths are silenced, the government's credibility will be lost." After publishing the summary, "Le Petit Parisien" said that the content of von Papen's speech was like this, which shows that the German government has different opinions on major issues, and it is no wonder that the German government hurriedly banned its publication. (Havas dispatch, 22nd)

Debt Issue: Germany Cannot Be Subdued by Threats, Willing to Sever Commercial Relations with Countries that Force a Clearing System, President of German Bank Publicly Expresses Demand to Recover Old Colonies 72

(Berlin) President Schacht of the Deutsche Bank hosted a tea party today to entertain diplomats and foreign newspaper representatives, stating that Germany intends to sever commercial relations with countries that force a clearing system on Germany. Schacht said that Germany's debt problem cannot be solved by power or coercion. The clearing system is equivalent to not paying for goods. This will reduce Germany's international trade to a very low level, eventually leading to a complete halt to international commercial relations. No one can believe that Germany will calmly endure it. If Great Britain establishes a clearing system, it will definitely greatly damage the trade between British territories and Germany. This is undoubtedly true. Schacht then proposed three ways to remedy the current difficult situation: (1) Return Germany's former colonies so that Germany can purchase raw materials with its own currency; (2) Give Germany more opportunities to increase its exports so that it can repay its debts; (3) Reduce the principal and interest of Germany's debts. Schacht also firmly stated that Germany's currency will never inflate. The German government is determined to maintain the stability of the mark, so the collapse of the German currency is definitely not a problem. (Reuters dispatch, 21st)

U.S. Treasury Department Begins Buying Silver, Gradually Purchasing with Funds to Stabilize Silver Prices 73

(Washington) Treasury Secretary Morgenthau announced today that the purchase of silver will be in accordance with the Congressional bill. Rumors of the government ceasing silver purchases have thus been dispelled. The Secretary stated, "We desire a healthy rise in silver prices, but we do not want the unstable fluctuations caused by market speculation as seen last summer. Once silver prices rise, we must stabilize them." Morgenthau further announced that the Treasury Department's silver purchasing plan has already commenced, with substantial amounts of silver being bought in New York and London. The funds used for purchasing silver come from the Treasury's exchange stabilization fund. Purchases began before the President signed the silver bill last Tuesday and are still ongoing. The Secretary declined to announce the amount of silver the government has purchased, but unofficial sources estimate it to be about 65 million ounces. The Secretary said that future purchases will depend entirely on the silver market; purchases will be made when prices are suitable. After the Secretary announced this news, silver advocates in Washington expressed strong support. Consequently, those who doubted that the government would actually implement silver purchases under permissible laws are now satisfied. (21st National Telegram)

(New York) The Treasury Department announced today that silver certificates issued for the purchase of silver will be based on the purchase price of the silver. This method will be used at least for the present. For example, if one million ounces of silver are purchased for $650,000, then $650,000 in silver certificates will be issued. Whether the Treasury Department will utilize the flexible provisions of the Silver Act to issue silver certificates at the inflated price of $1.29 per ounce is a policy issue to be determined in the future.

It is reported that the newly purchased silver will be used immediately to issue new silver certificates. However, the Treasury Department believes that this will not increase the currency in circulation but will instead use the silver certificates to withdraw an equivalent amount of Federal Reserve notes. (21st Reuters Telegram)

(New York) According to an official announcement today, 10,570,713 ounces of silver were withdrawn from the New York Commodities Exchange vault on Tuesday and Wednesday. The current vault balance is 92,136,662 ounces. According to well-informed financial sources, this silver has been transferred to the government vault, which is part of the Treasury Department's large-scale silver purchases in New York. Of the 1.45 million ounces of silver traded on the Commodities Exchange yesterday, approximately half was purchased by the Treasury Department. (21st National Telegram)

The Process of Negotiating Traffic on the Ping-Shen Railway 97

Agreements Reached in Yuguan and Dalian

North China Dispatch, The plan and detailed rules for traffic on the Ping-Shen railway have been agreed upon by both parties, and the official implementation awaits the China Travel Service and the Japanese International Tourist Bureau to directly contact each other regarding the joint establishment of a travel agency. After the China Travel Service received the official commission from the Ministry of Railways, the president of the company, Chen Xiangtao, reported to Yin Tong, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, this morning (21st), stating that he will soon head north to discuss everything. Regarding the traffic plan, after Yin Tong telegraphed the Ministry of Railways for instructions, it was decided that on the morning of the 28th at 9:00 AM, the timetable would be limited simultaneously in Beijing, Shanghai, Tianjin, and the Japanese side would publish it at the embassy. The name of our publishing agency has not yet been determined. After the plan is announced, implementation can begin, and the July 1st deadline will not be delayed again. Yin Tong will also issue a declaration when the plan is announced to explain the traffic matters. In addition, detailed implementation measures have been carefully formulated by the Beining Railway Bureau and compiled into a book. It will be announced at the same time as the plan is announced. Tracing back to the traffic issue, since Yin Tong, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, took office last winter, he drafted a plan in November due to the urging of the Japanese side. In May of this year, the urging from the Japanese side became more urgent, resulting in the Yuguan meeting on May 14th. However, that meeting only made preliminary exchanges of opinions on the traffic plan that had been drafted in the past. After the Yuguan meeting, Yin Tong took the results of the exchanges of opinions to Beijing and Shanghai for instructions. Then, Yin personally went to Dalian on the 13th of this month to negotiate in detail with Japanese embassy military attaché Shibayama and Manchukuo Railway representative Kougong, etc., and separately formulated detailed implementation rules, which were extremely detailed. They have recently been printed and bound into a book of over 200 pages. After both parties agreed, Yin returned to Tianjin on the 16th and convened responsible personnel from the accounting, transportation, and mechanical departments of the Beining Railway Bureau to re-discuss technical matters. They unanimously decided that only the issue of organizing the main agency remained to be discussed. Yin decided to invite relevant Chinese and Japanese personnel to Tianjin within this week for final discussions. The Chinese participants in this meeting will be representatives from the Ministry of Railways, Yin Tong, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, and the heads of various departments, and representatives from the China Travel Service. The Japanese participants will be representatives from the Kwantung Army, representatives from the Manchukuo Railway, and Suzuki, the Director of the International Tourist Bureau, and Shibayama, the military attaché of the Japanese embassy. Chen Xiangtao, the president of the China Travel Service, has been invited by Yin to come north. Prior to the Yuguan meeting, when the Japanese side initially raised the request for traffic, the Beijing side once sought Chen's consent regarding the main traffic matters. Therefore, Chen will also be summoned to come north for negotiations. Suzuki, the Director of the International Tourist Bureau of the Japanese side, etc., will arrive in Tianjin from Shenyang within days. The date for the implementation of traffic will be determined after the Tianjin meeting closes.

According to Yin Tong, "When I left Shanghai by ship for Dalian, Chairman Huang (Fu)'s nose disease had recovered. Because there are still matters to be discussed with the Central Government, the date of his trip north is uncertain. The traffic matter still needs to be discussed in Tianjin. When it will be implemented can only be determined after the discussions. At the same time, I will issue a statement in my personal capacity, detailing the process of handling traffic matters. The issue of the number of newly formed security teams in the war zone was agreed upon with the Japanese side when the Tanggu Truce Agreement was signed. It was agreed to train 9,000 people to enter the war zone. I participated in the meeting at the time and know it more accurately. Perhaps I can negotiate with the Japanese side again, and there will be no problem. As for the establishment of customs offices at various passes of the Great Wall, the Ministry of Finance is responsible for planning and resolving it. Because it is not my responsibility, I do not know the detailed measures." According to Japanese Embassy Military Attaché Shibayama, "The implementation of traffic is not far off. All issues in the war zone can be resolved gradually after the implementation of traffic. I will go to Tianjin in the next few days to negotiate with relevant parties (referring to the Japanese side)." (21st)

The Six-County Suppression Headquarters Concludes

Anqing Dispatch, Wang Xijun, Deputy Director of the Anhui Provincial Security Department and Commander-in-Chief of the Temporary Suppression of Bandits in Six Counties on the Border of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Provinces, was ordered in March of this year to go to Guangde on the Anhui border to organize the headquarters and supervise the suppression of bandits in various counties. The headquarters' suppression work has now been largely completed. He has also led all officers back to the province and returned to work at the department. (June 21st)

Legislative Yuan Passes the Savings Bank Law, Lottery Savings Should Be Strictly Prohibited Immediately, Ma Yinchu Issues Statement 99

The Legislative Yuan's Commercial Law Committee, considering that the General Banking Law has been passed by the Yuan Council and promulgated by the National Government for implementation, has drafted the Savings Bank Law, which was submitted and passed with amendments at the 64th meeting of the Yuan on the 22nd. The full text of the law consists of 17 articles, stipulating that savings banks cannot be established without approval, and lottery savings should be strictly prohibited immediately. For lottery savings deposits that have already been made before the implementation of this law, the measures for their closure will be drafted by the Ministry of Finance and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. The full text of the law, Ma Yinchu's statement, and the reasons for prohibiting lottery savings associations are recorded below.

Savings Bank Law 100

Article 1: Any entity that receives small deposits using compound interest methods is considered a savings bank. Any entity that meets the preceding criteria and is called a savings bank is also considered a savings bank.

Article 2: Savings banks shall be organized as limited liability companies. They shall not establish ordinary banks without the approval of the Ministry of Finance. According to the preceding regulation, they may concurrently operate savings bank businesses, but only if their fully paid-up capital reaches at least one million national currency units.

Article 3: The total capital of a savings bank shall be at least 500,000 national currency units. In areas with simple commerce, the capital amount stipulated in the preceding paragraph may be reduced with the approval of the Ministry of Finance, but it shall not be reduced to less than 100,000 national currency units.

Article 4: Savings banks shall not concurrently engage in other businesses besides the following: (1) Demand deposits that can be paid and withdrawn at any time; (2) Fixed-term deposits with lump-sum payment; (3) Installment deposits with lump-sum payment, or lump-sum deposits with installment payments, and fixed-term deposits with periodic interest payments; (4) Custody services; (5) Collection of payments and remittances; (6) Acting as agents for the purchase and sale of securities; (7) Collection and payment of funds for public welfare organizations and cooperatives; (8) Notification deposits for public welfare organizations and cooperatives.

Article 5: The amount of deposits in the first category of the preceding article shall not exceed 5,000 national currency units per household, and the total of all households shall not exceed four-tenths of the total deposit amount in each category of the preceding article. Checks shall not be used. The deposit amount in the second or third category of the preceding article shall not exceed 20,000 national currency units per household.

Article 6: The maximum term and highest interest rate for fixed-term deposits in savings banks shall be decided and restricted by the local banking association or its members, taking into account the circumstances, and submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval and record. If there is no banking association or its members, it shall be submitted by the local competent authority to the Ministry of Finance for approval and record.

Article 7: Savings banks shall not use their funds unless in accordance with the following methods when conducting the businesses stipulated in Article 4: (1) Purchasing government bonds, treasury bills, and other securities that are securely guaranteed and approved by the Ministry of Finance; (2) Lending with government bonds, treasury bills, and other securities that are securely guaranteed and approved by the Ministry of Finance as collateral; (3) Lending with continuous and real estate with guaranteed income as collateral; (4) Lending with fixed-term deposit certificates or passbooks from other banks as collateral; (5) Purchasing bills accepted by other banks; (6) Depositing in other banks; (7) Secured lending to rural cooperatives; (8) Lending with agricultural products as collateral.

Article 8: The total amount of securities issued by the same company that a savings bank accepts under items (1) and (2) of the preceding article shall not exceed one-tenth of the company's paid-up capital and the total amount of public bonds. The total amount of loans made by a savings bank under item (3) of the preceding article shall not exceed one-fifth of its total deposits. The total amount of loans made by a savings bank under item (4) of the preceding article shall not exceed one-fifteenth of its total deposits. The amount of bills purchased by a savings bank under item (5) of the preceding article shall not exceed one-twentieth of its total deposits. The amount of deposits a savings bank makes under item (6) of the preceding article shall not exceed one-fifteenth of its total deposits, except when government bonds, treasury bills, and other securities that are securely guaranteed and approved by the Ministry of Finance are used as collateral. When an ordinary bank concurrently operates a savings bank business, the preceding two paragraphs shall apply to the bills accepted by the bank department from the savings department and the amount of its deposits. The total amount of loans made by a savings bank under items (7) and (8) of the preceding article shall not be less than one-fifth of its total deposits.

Article 9: Savings banks shall deposit at least one-fourth of the total amount of savings deposits in government bonds, treasury bills, and other securely guaranteed assets with the Central Bank as collateral for repaying savings deposits. The total amount of deposits stipulated in the preceding paragraph shall be based on the total balance at the end of each year.

Article 10: The balance sheet and inventory of a savings bank shall be announced at least once every three months and reported to the Ministry of Finance or submitted by the local competent authority to the Ministry of Finance for record. The method of announcement stipulated in the preceding paragraph shall be specified in the articles of association of the savings bank.

Article 11: The Ministry of Finance may at any time send personnel or entrust the local competent authority to inspect the business content and the actual status of all assets of a savings bank. If savers with more than one-twentieth of the total deposit amount have doubts about the announcement and business stipulated in the preceding article, they may jointly petition the Ministry of Finance or the local competent authority to send personnel to jointly inspect with representatives elected by the savers.

Article 12: When an ordinary bank concurrently operates a savings bank business, all of its shareholders, directors, and supervisors shall be regarded as the shareholders, directors, and supervisors of the savings department.

Article 13: When an ordinary bank concurrently operates a savings bank business, it shall divide the assets and liabilities of the savings department and the bank department independently. The assets of the savings department shall not be affected by the bankruptcy of the bank department.

Article 14: Lottery savings shall be prohibited. The measures for the conclusion of lottery savings deposits that have already been handled before the implementation of this law shall be drafted by the Ministry of Finance and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval.

Article 15: When the assets of a savings bank are insufficient to repay the debts of each saver, the directors and supervisors shall bear joint and several unlimited liability. The joint and several unlimited liability of the directors and supervisors stipulated in the preceding paragraph shall not be released until two years after the registration of their resignation.

Article 16: Those who violate the provisions of Article 2 or Article 3 shall be fined between 1,000 and 5,000 yuan, and the Ministry of Finance may order them to suspend their business. Those who violate the provisions of Article 4, Article 5, Article 6, Article 7, Article 8, Article 9, Article 10, Article 12, or Article 13 shall be fined between 100 and 3,000 yuan for the directors, supervisors, and liquidators. Those who violate the provisions of Article 14 shall be sentenced to fixed-term imprisonment of not more than three years and fined between 1,000 and 5,000 yuan for the directors and supervisors, or for the shareholders if there are no directors and supervisors.

Article 17: This law shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. (To be continued)

Tianjin: Two Incidents in One Day; Head of Health Section of Beining Railway Bureau Assassinated; Three Bookstores Including Dacheng Bookstore Smashed 101

Tianjin Correspondence: Two unusual events occurred here today (19th). One was the assassination of Kang Mingzhen, the head of the health section of the Beining Railway Bureau, who was killed while passing through Asahi Street in the Japanese Concession. The other was that Hui people, believing that the sale of the book "Nian Gengyao Pacifying the West" by three bookstores including Dacheng Bookstore insulted their religion, gathered a crowd to smash the stores. The details are as follows:

Kang Mingzhen, the head of the health section of the Beining Railway Bureau, was 39 years old, a native of Haicheng, Liaoning. He graduated from the South Manchuria Railway Medical College and served as a physician at Qingdao Hospital and chief of the general affairs section of the Huludao Port Authority of the Beining Railway. After the September 18th Incident, he came to Tianjin. When the League of Nations Investigation Commission came to China, Kang served as the head of the Beidaihe Public Security Bureau. This spring, he was appointed as the head of the health section of the Beining Railway Bureau. His residence was at No. 5 Anding Lane, Guangdong Road, British Concession, Tianjin. Previously, Kang worked at the bureau and commuted to and from work by company car. After taking the position in the health section, it was inconvenient to commute by company car because his office was located on Xinda Road, Hebei, so he switched to rickshaws. This morning (19th) at 8:30, Kang took a rickshaw from his home to the office in Hebei, passing through Asahi Street in the Japanese Concession. At this time, a young thug, dressed as a worker, followed him on a bicycle. Kang did not notice that he was being followed because the street was a thoroughfare with many people coming and going. When he reached the front of the New Inn, the thug suddenly pulled out a pistol and aimed it at the back of Kang's head, firing once. The bullet entered through the upper part of the back of the head, exiting diagonally from the forehead without completely penetrating. Kang immediately bled profusely and fainted in the rickshaw. The thug immediately turned around and fled towards Rong Street. The rickshaw driver noticed something was wrong, looked back, but had already lost sight of the thug. He urgently summoned the police to send Kang to the Zhonghe Hospital for treatment. Due to excessive injuries, he died at around 11:00 AM. This afternoon, Nagao, the chief of the Japanese Concession Police Department, inspected the body at the hospital and told the family that he would do his best to search for the perpetrator. In the evening, the French Concession police arrested a young man at the Yuanxing Inn on Zhangzhuang Bridge, who was found to be in possession of a pistol. It is said that he is the perpetrator of this case, but the man does not admit it. Kang is survived by a wife and a concubine, and six children. His eldest son is 17 years old and studying in Beiping. He returned for the funeral tonight. His wife and one child each live in Haicheng, Liaoning. Only his concubine and three sons and one daughter live in Tianjin. It is reported that the reason for Kang's death is that Kang was an old member of the Kuomintang and still held a position in the Northeast Party Affairs Working Group in Beiping. He was required to go there once every Tuesday. Today happened to be Tuesday, and it is unknown why he did not go, but was assassinated. The authorities suspect a political background.

Dacheng Bookstore, located on Dahutong Street in Tianjin, is a branch of the Dacheng Bookstore in Shanghai. Recently, it has been selling the book "Nian Gengyao Pacifying the West," which has been selling very well. The content of the book describes how Hui people were treated when General Nian pacified the West. Hui people here believe that this insults their religion. Several days ago, some people secretly gathered and sent four or five people to Dacheng Bookstore disguised as customers, wanting to purchase 100 copies. The bookstore at that time boasted about the value of the book, with many false and incomplete claims, especially angering the people who came. At that time, there was no quarrel, and they paid and placed an order. Today at 8:30 PM, representatives from more than 20 mosques in Tianjin gathered in front of the bookstore on Dahutong Street and broke into the store, completely smashing the bookshelves upstairs and downstairs. The bookstore employees and staff all fled. One of them, Xu Liwu, was unable to escape and was beaten. Just as officers and police from the Third Precinct of the First District arrived to mediate, six Hui people including Liu Wenzhi came forward, willing to go to court, and were taken away by the police. The Hui people's remaining anger did not subside, and they went to Zhili Bookstore and Weiwen Bookstore on Beima Road, entering and carrying out the same smashing. One clerk from each of the two bookstores was injured. At this time, the provincial government and the Public Security Bureau heard the news and urgently sent personnel to stop them. Respected members of the Hui community also rushed to mediate, and the crowd dispersed. In the evening, the three bookstores each assessed the losses, which were considerable. Photos were taken and sent to various associations to appeal for assistance. Although the facts were as clear as day, the newspapers reporting on this event tonight all took a cautious attitude and were unwilling to publish the facts truthfully (19th).

Cantonese Merchants Oppose the Connection of the Guangzhou-Hankou and Guangzhou-Kowloon Railways; The Origin of the Re-emergence of the Issue of Railway Connection; Merchants from All Sectors Believe It is Harmful and Yields No Benefits 102

Guangzhou Correspondence: In order to complete its plan as the only port in South China, the Hong Kong government has long wanted to persuade the Guangdong government to connect the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway with the Guangzhou-Hankou Railway. The British have a broad vision, believing that when the Guangzhou-Hankou Railway is completed in the future, it will be the central route of China, connecting Pingjin in the north and reaching the Pearl River in the south. North-South commerce will rely on the transportation of this route and become more developed. In the future, the southern terminus of this route will be in Guangzhou, and its prosperity will be many times greater than it is today. Hong Kong is blocked by Guangzhou's hinterland. It is expected that Hong Kong's commerce with North China will be monopolized by Guangzhou. Therefore, the Hong Kong government proposed the connection of the Guangzhou-Kowloon and Guangzhou-Hankou Railways around 1923 and tried to persuade the Guangdong government to agree. Later, Chen Jiongming took charge of Guangdong's administration and Chen Xiru served as the provincial governor. Chen was a wealthy merchant in Hong Kong and belonged to the comprador class. He believed that the railway connection would benefit Hong Kong's commerce and forgot about the interests of Guangzhou's hinterland. There was an intention to negotiate, and a preliminary agreement for the railway connection was drafted. Unexpectedly, as soon as this proposal was announced, it was opposed by Cantonese merchants and groups from all walks of life, who strongly stated that the railway connection would cause hundreds of harms and no benefits to Guangdong Province. On the contrary, if this matter were to succeed, Hong Kong would become the southern terminus of the Guangzhou-Hankou Railway, and Guangzhou would become a wasteland. After fierce opposition from all walks of life, the Guangdong government, fearing public opinion, stopped the matter. People in Hong Kong and China, unable to achieve their goal, later changed their approach and persuaded the Guangdong side to lay tracks on Dexuan Road, so that the Guangzhou-Kowloon and Guangzhou-Hankou Railways could be connected invisibly. The Cantonese people saw through the inside story and strongly opposed it, and this proposal was shelved again. Until recently, Hong Kong has been affected by the global economic downturn, and Hong Kong's commerce has plummeted. At the beginning of the month, when the Hong Kong Chinese General Chamber of Commerce held its annual meeting, Chairman Huang Guangtian presented ten items in a plan to revitalize Hong Kong's commerce. The fourth item of the plan was to propose the connection of the Guangzhou-Kowloon and Guangzhou-Hankou Railways, believing that this move would greatly help revitalize Hong Kong's commerce. He also explained that according to the current Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway, the British section first saw a profit in 1930, with a profit of 138,767 yuan that year. This year it has increased to more than 711,000 yuan. The Chinese section loses 6,000 yuan per kilometer every year. The total track length is 140 kilometers, resulting in a total loss of 864,000 yuan per year. If the Guangzhou-Hankou and Guangzhou-Kowloon Railways are connected, the commercial benefits would be enormous, and the government could take the construction costs of the railway connection from the Boxer Indemnity, and so on. Since this matter was raised again, it has attracted the attention of the Cantonese people. On the 11th of this month, the Guangzhou Municipal Chamber of Commerce held a meeting to discuss this matter. Everyone believed that this matter was of great importance and that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce should solicit the opinions of the merchants and people of the entire city, submit them to the government, and ask for attention. Afterwards, the Guangzhou City Long-Distance Bus Association, the Rubber Industry Association, the Match Industry, the Piece Goods Industry, the Yarn Industry, the Hospitality Industry, and the Paper Industry Associations all believed that it was absolutely harmful and yielded no benefits, and strongly opposed it. Before long, merchants from the Leather Industry, Sauce and Condiment Industry, Tea House Industry, Western Medicine Industry, Silver Industry, Banking Industry, Fish Market, and North-South Trade Brokerage also continued to oppose it. Therefore, the proposal of Chairman Huang Guangtian of the Hong Kong Chinese General Chamber of Commerce to connect the railways can be said to be completely met with absolute opposition from the Cantonese merchants. If the government can comply with the request of the Cantonese people, this matter will be difficult to realize. In addition, Li Pan, the Director of the Guangzhou-Hankou (now renamed Guangzhou-Shaoguan) Railway Bureau, briefly expressed that the rumors of borrowing money from Britain with the connection of the Guangzhou-Kowloon and Guangzhou-Hankou Railways as a condition were completely unfounded. Xiao Focheng, a member of the Political Affairs Committee, also declared that he did not approve of the railway connection and that the government had no intention of accommodating the railway connection. (16th)

Qingpu: Fire in Dongmennei 103

At No. 126 Baoqing Street, Dongmennei of this city, a tenant surnamed Gu, nearly seventy years old, with impaired hearing and vision, usually cooked for himself and had no accidents. Unexpectedly, yesterday at noon, the kitchen of this man suddenly caught fire due to carelessness, and in an instant, flames burst through the roof. Since the man was unable to extinguish the fire, he rushed out and jumped out of the upstairs window, his head and face burned, barely alive. Fortunately, firefighters from various districts arrived at the scene one after another to put out the fire, and it was quickly extinguished, preventing it from spreading to neighboring houses. The injured Mr. Gu was sent to the public hospital for treatment by police car. However, due to the severity of his injuries, he died at 3:00 PM.

Chairman Chiang, in order to reorganize the Civil Defense Corps of Jiangsu and Jiangxi provinces, specially appointed Luo Yi, Hou Zhiqin, Wang Shihai and three others as Jiangsu-Jiangxi District Civil Defense Corps Inspection Commissioners. Maoyuan Pawnshop Declares Closure 105

Due to the recent economic depression in Suzhou and the bankruptcy of rural areas, the business of pawnshops has declined, suffering heavy losses, and several have been unable to maintain their operations and have closed. Now, Maoyuan Pawnshop in Bao Yaqian, also an old pawnshop with more than 20 years of history, has declared closure due to business failure. It has been reported to the county government yesterday. Dasheng Pawnshop in Tieping Lane is also about to declare closure.

Wuxi: Dispute Over the Management of the Park 106

Wuxi Park has been managed by a park management committee separately organized by the Municipal Management Committee, which manages all income and expenditure and various constructions. Recently, the Municipal Management Committee was ordered to be abolished, and disputes arose between various parties regarding the right to manage the park, which are recorded as follows: (1) Elders such as Hua Yishan cited the history of the park, pointing out that the park is not a district property but belongs to the county. Based on past history, a board of directors should be organized by local gentry and former park committee members to manage it. (2) The First District Office believed that Sun Zuji, when he was the county magistrate, had once managed it by the District Office, and that since the park is in the urban area, it naturally belongs to the municipal property, and the municipal property is the district property, which should be managed by the District Office. (3) The County Education Bureau believed that the park is one of the social education facilities and should be managed by the educational authorities, and formulated an improvement plan, preparing to take over. The above points have aroused deep concern among local people, but it is unknown who will win in the end.

New Life Movement Exhibition 107

The New Life Movement Promotion Association, a county-run social education institution in this county, has recently been actively preparing to hold a New Life Movement Exhibition, which has been scheduled to open tomorrow (24th) and last until the 26th. The venue is in the County Library in the city center. The content of the exhibition is divided into ten groups: 1. General Group, 2. Clothing Group, 3. Food and Drink Group, 4. Housing Group, 5. Action Group, 6. Health Group, 7. Education Group, 8. Entertainment Group, 9. Work Group, 10. Reference Group. Each group has models, colored paintings, photos and explanations. The Second Day of the High School Joint Entrance Examination 108

The High School Graduation Joint Entrance Examination of the Third District of Jiangsu Province was held yesterday for the second day. At 8:00 AM, it was held on time at the Jiangsu Xishan Normal School. There were two sessions throughout the day, arithmetic in the morning and geography in the afternoon. The test questions were: How many necessary convenient roads are there within China that must pass through foreign countries to get to another part of China? Briefly describe them. Which countries border our country along the border? Briefly explain the border situation. Japan has always called our three northeastern provinces its lifeline and has been planning to relocate farmers for many years, but it has been difficult to achieve its wish. Briefly describe the obstacles from a natural perspective. List twelve important ports of transportation and military facilities from Western Europe to the Far East ruled by the British Empire, etc. The two heads of the county bureau both came out to invigilate, and it was completed at 5:00 PM in the afternoon. In order to facilitate the provincial department's grading, all the test papers were specially hired and sent to the province that night.

Changshu: Public Memorial for Two National Heroes 109

Wang Tieqian and Pan Ming, two anti-Japanese national heroes from this county during the Jiajing period (of the Ming Dynasty), led the civil defense corps out of the city to meet the invaders when Japanese pirates repeatedly invaded the area. Wang and Pan both died in this battle. (According to historical records, Wang was the magistrate of this county at that time, while Pan was from Luyuan in this county and was a Jinshi graduate.) A Double Loyalty Shrine was built in front of the Liwang Palace in the city. Later, due to the passage of time, the historical traces of the two heroes were almost lost. Later, the Education Department ordered the county to repair the Wang-Pan Double Loyalty Shrine, which once again attracted attention. Now the Double Loyalty Shrine has been completely renovated. The county party department decided that July 5th, the date of martyrdom of the two heroes, will be the date to hold the first memorial service in conjunction with various agencies to honor their loyalty and publicize the deeds of the two heroes to the public.

Zhenjiang: Cases of Each County Involving Smoking and Opium Are To Be Handled By The Provincial Anti-Opium Council 110

Yu Jingtang, the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs of Jiangsu Province, recently ordered the county governments to say: "After investigation, the Anti-Opium Committee of this province has been established. Article 2 of its organizational charter stipulates that the Provincial Anti-Opium Committee shall carry out the orders of the Provincial Government, take charge of the anti-opium affairs of the entire province, and supervise the subordinate agencies. The Provincial Anti-Opium Committee is in charge of all anti-opium cases as mandated by orders. Therefore, the Provincial Anti-Opium Committee is responsible for taking charge of the whole province and has the right to supervise subordinate agencies. Hereafter, all anti-opium cases in this province should be handled by the Provincial Anti-Opium Committee in order to assign responsibility. In addition to sending to all entities, it is hereby ordered to the county head that they shall comply accordingly."

Nantong: Trial Opens for Alteration of Aviation Lottery Ticket Case 111

The Nantong Court Prosecutor's Office, regarding the case of the third-term aviation lottery ticket winning the fifth prize, serial number 227404, which was altered from serial number 227104, has concluded its investigation. It has filed a public lawsuit against Yu Chongwei, the president of the Bank of China, for embezzlement of the prize money, and against Yang Youheng, the recipient of the prize money, for false accusation. It has also filed a public lawsuit against Shi Mingqing, Fan Ji, and others who held the ticket for forgery. The criminal court held a public trial on the 21st. Because Yu Chongwei, the president of the Bank of China, was in Shanghai and had not returned, Shi Mingqing had been released on bail and had not arrived, and Fan Ji had not been apprehended, the court ordered the trial to be adjourned.

Hangzhou: Big Fire in Jianggan Claims Four Lives 113

The weather in Hangzhou has been dry recently, and fires have been frequent. At 3:40 AM on the 21st, a fire broke out at the home of Xu Qingyu at No. 9 Chailu Road, Jianggan, due to carelessness with cigarette butts. Neighbors woke up to the fire, and the fire spread rapidly, causing great chaos. Firefighters from the Yilong team rushed to put out the fire, which was finally extinguished after more than an hour. The thatched houses from No. 6 to No. 11 were all burned to the ground. During the fire, Zhu Ji, a 54-year-old resident of No. 8, his wife Yi, and their six children were lost in the thick smoke. Zhu Ji, his wife, and their three-year-old daughter A Ju all died in the fire. His wife was eight months pregnant. They were burned into charred wood, a tragic sight. The court sent officials to inspect the scene and provide coffins for burial.

<The Shanghai Municipal Council's Rickshaw Committee's Report on Improvement Plans, Seeking Fair Criticism by Clarifying Facts, Rickshaw Rental Reduction of Ten Cents Starting in August P]> 119

Since its establishment, the Rickshaw Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council in the Public Concession has been actively conducting investigations. Sixteen reform measures were agreed upon and submitted to the Board of Directors for discussion. Thirteen of these measures were passed and announced for implementation. However, the rickshaw owners have consistently and strongly opposed them. Yesterday, the committee specially invited reporters from various newspapers to report the truth of the matter so that the public could understand the facts and offer fair criticism to eliminate long-standing malpractices.

The committee members present yesterday were Zhu Maocheng, Massey, and Director Wang Zhiren. Mr. Zhu first reported on the formation of the committee, stating briefly that the organization of the Rickshaw Committee began in September of last year. At that time, there was widespread criticism and suggestions regarding the corruption of rickshaws in the concession. The Municipal Council then accepted these suggestions and organized this committee, with Massey, Jiang Yiping, Zhu Maocheng, Harrison, and Bo Jian Tuo as members. They began to investigate this issue to determine if improvements were necessary. The investigation revealed many malpractices, so sixteen reform proposals were immediately agreed upon and submitted to the Board of Directors for discussion. As a result, thirteen measures were passed and scheduled to be implemented on July 1st. Unexpectedly, the rickshaw owners strongly opposed them and engaged in malicious propaganda. The committee's role is merely to offer suggestions. If the rickshaw owners have any concerns, they are welcome to meet sincerely, and the committee is willing to promote implementation through peaceful means. Therefore, although the Council has adopted the measures, they have not been enforced with force, and rickshaw rentals have been reduced.

Currently, rickshaw pullers have to pay a rental fee of up to fourteen small silver coins each day, so that the income from their daily labor is almost entirely extorted by the rickshaw owners. According to a careful investigation by this committee, the average income of each rickshaw puller is only 9.23 yuan per month, which must support the needs of several family members. The hardship of their lives can be imagined. From a humanitarian perspective, rickshaw rentals should also be reduced. The Municipal Council passed a regulation setting the rickshaw rental at eight small silver coins per day. Although it was scheduled to be implemented on July 1st, this committee, out of consideration for the rickshaw owners, requested a temporary postponement. It also suggested that starting from August 1st, the daily rickshaw rental should be changed to ten small silver coins, and only be reduced to eight coins from January 1st of the following year. In this way, the gradual reduction should not cause any difficulties.

Key Points of Improvement

Mr. Zhu also stated that the improvement items suggested by this committee include several aspects: (1) Reduce the rickshaw rental to eight coins. Although this has already been passed, for the sake of facilitating implementation, it will first be reduced to ten coins from August 1st. (2) Licenses are not allowed to be resold. (3) Licenses must be obtained by the rickshaw owners themselves, and the rickshaw owners must also obtain rickshaw owner certificates. This matter has already been implemented. (4) Rickshaw pullers will also be issued licenses, because currently, when rickshaw pullers violate regulations, they are often subjected to insults such as beatings and license confiscation. In the future, if there are violations, their license numbers will be recorded for prosecution, and arbitrary kicking and beating will not be allowed, in order to enhance their dignity. (5) Improve the style of rickshaws to make them economical, lightweight, durable, and comfortable. All of these are intended to seek improvements in all aspects. As for the stipulated rickshaw fares, the purpose is also to increase the income of rickshaw pullers and improve their living standards, but it will not be forcibly implemented. However, a standard will be set to avoid disputes over fares between rickshaw pullers and passengers.

Relief Work

Finally, Mr. Wang Zhiren reported on the committee's relief work plan, stating that the goal is to achieve self-help for rickshaw pullers through the supervision and assistance of the committee. Therefore, it is planned to organize a rickshaw pullers' mutual aid society. For example, when the rickshaw rental is reduced by ten cents, eleven cents will be collected, and the extra cent will be used as funds to be deposited in a designated bank. There are currently 10,000 rickshaws in the concession, which can generate about 15,000 yuan per month, or about 180,000 yuan per year. The Municipal Council will appoint three supervisors, and representatives from various charitable organizations will be invited to a meeting to discuss and implement various projects, such as medical care and hygiene for rickshaw pullers, education for their children, public dormitories, death benefits, and proper entertainment. It is also hoped that rickshaw pullers will be able to manage and operate themselves with the existing funds, which can be carried out gradually year by year. The benefits to rickshaw pullers will definitely be significant.
