Tang Youren took the night express train to Beijing yesterday.

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Submits a Request

To Clearly Define the Date for Abolishing Harsh and Miscellaneous Taxes and Fees

And Requests a Reduction in Export Tax Rates

Based on the resolutions of the Fifth General Assembly of Representatives, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce specially submitted a request to the Executive Yuan yesterday to clearly define the date for abolishing harsh and miscellaneous taxes and fees. The original text is recorded as follows:

A request for the matter of submitting a request. The association held the Fifth General Assembly of Members on the 17th of this month. According to the joint proposal of representatives Ye Jiaxing, Cheng Yujie, Yuan Hongjun, Ma Jisheng, etc., a request was submitted to the government to clearly define the date for implementing the abolition of harsh and miscellaneous taxes and fees, and to request a reduction in export taxes. The proposal stated that, "At present, all industries are declining, and commerce and industry are in distress. People feel overwhelmed by the various harsh and miscellaneous taxes and fees of the country. At the same time, the national finances are on the verge of exhaustion, and there is a sense that there is nothing left to exploit. This abnormal contradiction is the most profound and serious problem in our country today, which urgently needs to be addressed and resolved. Although the central government has issued orders to abolish harsh and miscellaneous taxes and fees, implementation still requires time. Export trade, in particular, should be supported. In order to consider the interests of both parties, it is proposed that the central government quickly define the date for implementing the abolition and appropriately reduce the export trade tax to alleviate the suffering of merchants and people. At the same time, implement a state monopoly on cigarettes to increase revenue and enrich the national treasury. Is this appropriate? A request is submitted for public deliberation."

It was found that the association had previously received a telegram stating that all harsh and miscellaneous taxes and fees would be abolished in stages within the second half of this year. After reporting this to the General Assembly for discussion, it was believed that the proposal regarding the implementation date for abolishing harsh and miscellaneous taxes and fees had been resolved by the Executive Yuan, which was determined to supervise and urge the provinces to strictly adhere to the deadlines. The people would be freed from their suffering, and the time should not be far off. All proposals to increase the tax rate on consumable cigarettes to compensate for the reduction in export taxes should be considered by the central government as a means of improving tax revenue. It was resolved that the case should be forwarded to the Executive Yuan for review, approval, and implementation, which would be in the public interest.

China Aviation Corporation Cables to the US

To Change the Order to New Douglas Dolphin Aircraft

The Longhua Seaplane Port is Underway with Land Acquisition

New Southwest and Kangzang Routes are Actively Being Planned

The Shanghai-Guangdong Route is Expected to Resume Within the Year

The China Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Guangdong route has been temporarily suspended since the accident involving the Sikorsky aircraft. The company had previously cabled to the United States to order two new Commodore aircraft. According to Mr. Dai Enji, General Manager of the company, who spoke to a reporter from Shen Shi News Agency, they have now cabled to the United States to change the order to two new Douglas Dolphin aircraft. The route is expected to resume within the year. At the same time, preparations are being made for the opening of the new Southwest and Kangzang routes. The details are as follows:

Changing the Order to New Aircraft for Route Resumption Within the Year

According to Mr. Dai, the previous order for Commodore aircraft from the United States was decided by the Board of Directors. However, the structure of the aircraft is complex, and construction is time-consuming. Moreover, it is a model from four or five years ago in the United States, which is slightly slower compared to the latest aircraft. For the convenience of passengers, the company recently cabled to the United States to change the order to two of the latest Douglas Dolphin aircraft. Each of these aircraft can carry eighteen people and has two engines. The fuselage is sturdy, and the speed is the highest, averaging 150 miles per hour. The American side is actively rushing to build the aircraft after receiving the cable. It is expected to be completed in August and shipped to China. Around mid-October, after adding parts and test flights, it will be formally used within December to resume the Shanghai-Guangdong route. According to Mr. Dai, although these two aircraft are sufficient for the Shanghai-Guangdong route, in order to prevent accidents and develop business, they will continue to purchase one more aircraft. They will cable to the American side again soon to request another aircraft to be built at the same time as the previous two and shipped to Shanghai.

Longhua Airport is Underway with Land Acquisition

For the sake of improving flight equipment, the company plans to expand Longhua Airport. This has been reported in various newspapers. According to Mr. Dai yesterday, this project is extremely large and cannot be undertaken by the company alone. Moreover, there may be complications when purchasing land from the people. It is necessary to request assistance from the local authorities. Currently, the company has sent personnel to survey and negotiate land purchase procedures with the surrounding farmers. A small amount has recently been purchased. It is planned to gradually expand the airport and then proceed with the construction of rest areas, restaurants, and other facilities in order to realize the original plan.

Planning New Southwest and Kangzang Routes

Mr. Dai continued, "Aviation transportation is extremely important to the inland. Unfortunately, the company's current strength is insufficient and cannot be realized one by one. However, we are actively planning for this and striving to open the new Southwest and Kangzang routes at the same time in the shortest possible time. Once the planning has made some progress, we will still purchase aircraft from the American side for use."

Special Committee of the Rickshaw Industry

Scheduled to Host Various Sectors

To Report on Objections to the Shanghai Municipal Council's Rickshaw Committee Regulations

Advise Rickshaw Owners to Seriously Implement Resolutions of the General Assembly

The Special District Office of the Rickshaw Industry, after establishing a special committee in opposition to the regulations of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Rickshaw Committee, held its second meeting at the association at 9 PM last night. (2) Publish a special issue, the content of which will describe the steps taken by rickshaw owners to help rickshaw pullers, in order to clarify matters to all sectors of society. (3) The special committee will regularly host the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, the Public Concession Taxpaying Chinese Association, the French Concession Taxpaying Chinese Association, all executive and supervisory committee members, news reporters from major newspapers, and leaders from all sectors to report on the progress and seek assistance from all sectors of society. (4) In the future, the special committee will hold a meeting every night from 8 PM to 9 PM, and the meeting will be adjourned at 10 PM.

The Schedule for Two Railways is Revised

To be Implemented from July 1st

However, the Songhu Section and the Yongshao Section Will Remain the Same

The Schedules of Railways Throughout the Country Have Also Been Set

The schedules of railways throughout the country have been revised in accordance with the resolutions of the Joint Transportation Schedule Conference. The standard is the Shanghai-Ping Through Train, which is interconnected. The revisions will be implemented from July 1st. The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways have been set, but the schedules of the Songhu Section and the Yongshao Section will remain the same. The new schedule is listed below:

Circulars from the Two Railway Bureaus

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways issued a circular announcing the revised schedule. The circular stated that in order to comply with the resolutions of the National Joint Transportation Schedule Conference, the schedules of railways throughout the country should be interconnected based on the schedule of the 301st and 302nd Shanghai-Ping Through Trains, and the main trains on various routes should also be connected. The revised departure times of all trains on the two railways will be implemented simultaneously from July 1st as scheduled. The new pocket schedule has been sent to the printer and will be completed soon. At that time, please inquire at the Shanghai Railway Business Office, the Shanghai Nanshi Business Branch, the Nanjing Business Office, and the information desks at major stations, or ask the stationmasters at various stations. This announcement is made. As for the Shanghai-Ping Through Train and the schedules of the Beining and Jinpu Railways, the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Bureaus have cabled those railway bureaus to quickly set them and send them to Shanghai. As for other railways, although the schedules have been decided, the timetables have not been printed and sent to Shanghai.

County Land Price Tax to be Levied at the Beginning of Next Month

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance Strictly Pursues Overdue Taxes

The Shanghai County Government, with the end of the 22nd year approaching and the first installment of the 23rd year's land price tax urgently needing preparation for collection, has decided to set up counters for collection at the beginning of next month. Yesterday, it ordered the tax collection office to comply. The county government has now received instructions from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, stating briefly that the assessment of the collection of field taxes for the 22nd year is based on the end of June of the 23rd year as the assessment period. This time, there is a grace period of two years, which can be included before the end of June, which is out of consideration. The assessment must be carried out on schedule, and efforts should be made to strictly pursue taxes within the regular and extended periods. Don't be negligent in pursuing the taxes, lest you be punished. After receiving the order, the county government immediately supervised the tax collection office and the various tax collectors to actively collect taxes and pursue them within the prescribed time limit.

Ministry of Finance Designates Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax for Local Collection

Following the Resolutions of the National Financial Conference

To be Implemented from July 1st

The tobacco and alcohol license tax originally belonged to the nature of business tax, and was collected by the provincial and municipal stamp tobacco and alcohol tax bureaus under the Ministry of Finance. Recently, after discussion at the National Financial Conference, it was decided that from July 1st, the license tax will be designated for collection by local governments. The Ministry of Finance specially consulted the provincial and municipal governments and provincial financial departments for reference, and ordered the provincial stamp tobacco and alcohol tax bureaus to stop collection by the end of June. The original text of the consultation order is recorded as follows:

Consultation to the Provincial and Municipal Governments

All financial departments and financial bureaus, the case in question is that the tobacco and alcohol license tax is inherently a business nature. In June of the 20th year of the Republic of China, the National Government promulgated the Business Tax Law, which stipulates in Article 2 that "of the tobacco and alcohol license tax collected by the central government, 10% should be retained by the central government, and the rest should be allocated to the provinces and cities as local revenue." The provincial stamp tobacco and alcohol tax bureaus directly under the Ministry have been collecting taxes in accordance with the regulations, and the payments have been allocated separately. At this time, the Ministry convened the National Financial Conference to address the issue of reducing the field tax surcharge in various provinces and cities and abolishing harsh miscellaneous taxes and fees, and the methods of compensation. Because there was concern that local financial resources would be insufficient, the conference resolved to allocate the entire tobacco and alcohol license tax to the localities, to be collected by the localities, in order to increase income. And according to the Secretariat of the Conference, the resolution was submitted for approval. The Ministry also added verification. This tobacco and alcohol license tax, according to the provisions of the Business Tax Law, should have been collected by the central government, but since there are previous circumstances, the Ministry, in order to adjust local finances, should allow it to be changed to local self-management, for the convenience of tax collection. It is now decided that from July 1st of this year, the allocation will be implemented. Please ask your provincial and municipal governments to instruct the financial department (bureau) to comply with the central laws and regulations, to continue to collect taxes. The required spring, summer, autumn and winter seasons tobacco and alcohol wholesale or retail licenses will still be printed by the Ministry, and the department (bureau) should be ordered to list the detailed number, prepare printing costs, and submit to the Ministry for use, in order to unify and facilitate assessment. In addition to consulting separately with the provincial and municipal governments and financial departments, to receive and start operations from the beginning of the 21st year, and issuing a notice to the provincial stamp tobacco and alcohol tax bureaus to instruct their subordinate branches to end the assessment of tobacco and alcohol license tax matters by the deadline, and report to the Executive Yuan to be presented to the National Government for approval and record, a copy of the Provisional Regulations and Implementation Rules for Tobacco and Alcohol Business License Tax is enclosed for your provincial and municipal governments to check and process. It is still hoped that you will reply. As for the handling after receipt, and how to reduce the burden on the people, please also instruct to handle earnestly and report to the Ministry at any time for verification.

Order to Various Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureaus

Also instructing the provincial stamp tobacco and alcohol tax bureaus, the case in question is that the tobacco and alcohol license tax is inherently a business nature. In June of the 20th year of the Republic of China, the National Government promulgated the Business Tax Law, which stipulates in Article 2 that "of the tobacco and alcohol license tax collected by the central government, 10% should be retained by the central government, and the rest should be allocated to the provinces and cities as local revenue." The implementation has been carried out accordingly. At this time, the Ministry convened the National Financial Conference to address the issue of reducing the field tax surcharge in various provinces and cities and abolishing harsh miscellaneous taxes and fees, and the methods of compensation. Because there was concern that local financial resources would be insufficient, the conference resolved to allocate the entire tobacco and alcohol license tax to the localities, to be collected by the localities, in order to increase income. And according to the Secretariat of the Conference, the resolution was submitted for approval. The Ministry also added verification. This tobacco and alcohol license tax, according to the provisions of the Business Tax Law, should have been collected by the central government, but since there are previous circumstances, the Ministry, in order to adjust local finances, should allow it to be changed to local self-management, for the convenience of tax collection. It is now decided that from July 1st of this year, the allocation will be implemented, and the provincial and municipal governments should be handed over to continue collecting taxes in accordance with the central laws and regulations. The bureau should be ordered to telegraph its subordinate branches to end all matters related to the assessment of tobacco and alcohol license tax matters by June 30th of this year. All autumn license taxes for this year must not be collected again. The bureau's remaining licenses of various types and quantities should be made into a clear list and submitted by the bureau to the Ministry, and it is not allowed to be left outside, in order to prevent abuses. Violators will be dealt with for unclear cases. In addition to notifying the provincial stamp tobacco and alcohol tax bureaus to end on schedule, and consulting separately with the provincial governments and financial departments, to receive and start operations from the beginning of the 23rd year, and report to the Executive Yuan to be presented to the National Government for approval and record, it is appropriate to order you to report on the handling of the situation for verification. This order.

Tax Office Interpretation

Regulations on the Collection of Special Tax on Wheat Flour

All Wheat Flour Not Made from Wheat by Machine is Exempted from Tax

Yesterday's instructions to all district unified tax bureaus to be informed

The Ministry of Finance Tax Office in this port previously requested an interpretation of the ambiguity of the word "wheat flour" from the Customs Administration regarding the collection of special tax on wheat flour. Yesterday, a reporter from Shen Shi News learned that the Tax Office has replied to the Customs Administration and instructed all district bureaus under its jurisdiction to be informed. The original order stated, "The Customs Administration's Document No. 1780 was approved, stating that, according to the report of the Acting Tax Commissioner, it is necessary to clearly define whether the word 'wheat flour' refers to wheat or includes various wheat flours, in order to distinguish between tariff exemptions and levies. Please provide a reply for reference." "The regulations on the collection of special tax on wheat flour stipulate in Article 3 that all non-machine-made wheat flour bran and wheat used as raw materials are not subject to tax." The target of taxation specifically refers to wheat flour bran made from wheat raw materials by machine, and the meaning is very clear. In other words, all wheat bran that is not made from wheat as raw material and is not made by machine is not subject to tax, so there is no doubt. However, the wheat flour item was originally established for the purpose of offsetting the customs duties, in order to levy the customs duties on raw material wheat and change it to a special tax on wheat flour. When the business was opened, the wheat duties had not yet been abolished. Various wheat flour factories purchased raw material wheat, and the Ministry issued tax exemption certificates to give special exemptions from customs duties. Other wheat that was not used by the various wheat flour factories and other types of wheat still had to pay customs duties in order to equalize the burden. Later, before the abolition of customs duties, part of the wheat duties was universally exempted. Since various types

Suitable Financial Revenue and Expenditure in Hubei Province 120

The finances of Hubei Province were originally very difficult. In the 22nd year [of the Republic, i.e., 1933], every effort was made to economize, and revenue and expenditure were balanced. In addition, old debts of approximately 3.5 million yuan were repaid. The budget for the 23rd year [i.e., 1934] has also been decided. All revenue is based on the actual receipts of the previous year as a standard. On the expenditure side, in addition to increasing expenditure on projects by several hundred thousand yuan, there is no increase in administrative expenses. The revenue and expenditure are roughly the same as in the previous year. As for the 70 million yuan Class A debt and over 1 million yuan in bank debts owed by the Hubei Provincial Government, since being restructured, they have now been completely paid off and will soon be finalized.

Re-establishing the Hubei River Police 121

The Hubei River Police were extremely corrupt. Since I took office, I immediately ordered the River Police to be suspended and used the original River Police funds to accumulate savings, ordering two gunboats and six patrol boats from the Jiangnan Shipyard of the Navy. The original old ships of the River Police will also be renovated, and a River Police Training Institute will be established to train personnel and re-establish the River Police. The first phase of the plan is scheduled to begin in September. As for the eight new ships being built, they should be completed by the end of the month. The Jiangnan Shipyard of the Navy is a public institution, so they work diligently, and the construction costs are also quite fair.

This Year's Floods Will Not Lead to Disaster 122

Currently in Hubei Province, apart from small groups of remnant bandits still existing on the borders, the interior is free of bandit activity. All the dikes throughout the province can also be fully completed before the high-water season. This year's water level is about six to seven feet lower than last year, and the floods will not lead to disaster. Hubei Province has suffered from banditry and floods for years in a row, and the rural economy was almost bankrupt. Fortunately, last year's harvest was good, and the livelihoods of the farmers were slightly improved. Based on observations of the weather and geography this year, it is hoped that the vitality of the rural areas can be restored.

Managing and Operating Inland River Merchant Ships on Behalf of Owners 123

Starting in March of this year, Hubei Province implemented the management and operation of inland river merchant ships on behalf of owners, and the results have been very good so far. At the beginning of the implementation, merchants and the public had some misunderstandings. Subsequently, a supervisory committee was established, composed of the chairman of the Hankou Bankers' Association, the chairman of the Hubei Provincial Federation of Commerce, two representatives of shipping merchants, and one representative each from the Provincial Government's Finance Department and Construction Department. The powers are (1) supervising accounting; (2) reviewing business plans and reports; (3) suggesting improvements. Since its implementation, business has been progressing day by day, prices are also one-third cheaper than before, the time is accurate, and all the bad habits of the shipping industry have been eliminated. On the one hand, shipping merchants are given guarantees, and on the other hand, passengers are provided with convenience. Government and merchants cooperate wholeheartedly, and misunderstandings are completely eliminated.

Administrative Orders Decided to be Unified 124

The Hubei Provincial Government is currently preparing to start construction of new buildings to be used as a joint office. It has also been decided to first implement unified administrative orders before the provincial system is reformed. Hereafter, orders to all levels of government will be issued in the name of the Provincial Government. The various departments can only issue orders to their subordinate agencies. All measures have been submitted to the headquarters for approval and implementation.

Chiang's Trip to Hangzhou Has No Fixed Date 125

Chairman Chiang will be going to Hangzhou in the next few days, but the date has not been determined. As for whether he will come to Shanghai or return to Fenghua, nothing has been heard.

Regulations for the Yuping Railway Public Bonds - The Ministry of Railways Obtains Order for Promulgation - Borrowing Banks Decide to Form a Loan Syndicate 126

The Ministry of Railways, in order to construct the railway from Yushan to Pingxiang in Jiangxi Province, after being approved by the National Government and in conjunction with the Ministry of Finance, issued 12 million yuan in Yuping Railway Public Bonds, stipulating an annual interest rate of 6%, with the local salt surtax items allocated by the central government to Jiangxi as a fund for repaying principal and interest. It was issued from June 1st. The regulations for these public bonds were formulated and promulgated by the National Government yesterday and ordered by the Ministry of Railways to be notified to the two railway bureaus. The borrowing banks have also decided to form a bond loan syndicate. The details are recorded below.

Order from the Ministry of Railways 127

The Dagong News Agency reported that the two railway administration bureaus received an order from the Ministry of Railways yesterday, which stated: "Referring to Order No. 2995 from the Executive Yuan, which includes Order No. 344 from the National Government, it has been determined that the Regulations for the Yuping Railway Public Bonds of the 23rd Year of the Republic [i.e., 1934] have now been formulated and are hereby promulgated and should be immediately enforced. Besides a separate order, a copy of the regulations and attached schedule are enclosed for your information, and you are to instruct your subordinates to be informed as well." Upon receiving this, apart from a separate order, a copy of the original attached regulations and schedule are enclosed for your information, and you are to instruct your subordinates to be informed as well. This order.

Public Bond Regulations 128

Article 1: The National Government, in order to construct the railway from Yushan to Pingxiang in Jiangxi Province, issues public bonds jointly by the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Railways, named the Yuping Railway Public Bonds of the 23rd Year of the Republic [i.e., 1934]. Article 2: The fixed amount of this public bond is 12 million yuan in national currency. Article 3: This public bond is issued on June 1st, the 23rd Year of the Republic [i.e., 1934]. Article 4: The interest rate for this public bond is fixed at 6% per annum, with interest paid twice a year at the end of May and the end of November. Article 5: This public bond is designated to use 1.93 million yuan annually from the local salt surtax items allocated by the central government to Jiangxi as a fund for repaying principal and interest. The Ministry of Finance is to order the Salt Revenue Audit General Office to transfer the order to the West Bank Audit Office. Starting from the date of repayment of the Jiangxi Financial Reorganization Bonds in May of the 24th Year of the Republic [i.e., 1935], the West Bank Audit Office will remit the funds monthly according to the plan to the Audit General Office for deposit in the Central Bank, listed in the account managed by the National Debt Fund Management Committee, for the payment of principal and interest upon maturity. Article 6: This public bond will begin repaying principal from the end of November in the 24th Year of the Republic [i.e., 1935], with principal repaid once every six months. From the first to the eighth time, 5% will be drawn each time. From the ninth to the twelfth time, 7% will be drawn each time. From the thirteenth to the sixteenth time, 8% will be drawn each time. By the end of May in the 32nd Year of the Republic [i.e., 1943], all principal will be fully repaid. The aforementioned principal repayment will be executed by lottery 20 days before each maturity date. Article 7: This public bond designates the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications as the institutions for paying principal and interest. Article 8: The face value of this public bond is fixed at 10,000 yuan, 1,000 yuan, and 100 yuan. Article 9: This public bond is in the form of bearer bonds. Article 10: This public bond is issued at 98, that is, 98 yuan is actually received for every 100 yuan, and the interest due from the date of payment to May 31st in the 24th Year of the Republic [i.e., 1935] can be deducted in advance. Article 11: This public bond can be freely bought, sold, and mortgaged. When it is necessary to pay a deposit for official business, it can be used as collateral and can also be used as a guarantee reserve for banks. Article 12: Anyone who forges, damages, or uses this public bond for a long time will be punished by the judicial authorities according to law. Article 13: These regulations will be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Contract to be Signed 129

The Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Railways have mortgaged the first phase of railway construction public bonds and the Yuping Railway Public Bonds of the 23rd Year of the Republic [i.e., 1934], each with a face value of 12 million yuan, to a syndicate organized by the Bank of China and other banks in Shanghai for 16 million yuan, of which 8 million yuan is guaranteed by the syndicate for purchasing materials from German firms for the construction of the Yuping Railway. The interest rate is stipulated at 8%. The draft contract has been signed and can be formally signed after the German person sent by the German firm to Germany to purchase materials returns to Shanghai.

Distribution Agreed Upon 130

Although the draft contract for the loan of the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Zhejiang Xingye Bank, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, and other banks in Shanghai for the construction of the Yuping Railway by the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Railways was signed by a representative of the Bank of China with the two ministries, the distribution of the loan amounts to each bank was not decided at that time. It was not until recently that the banks formally agreed, with the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Central Bank receiving the largest shares.

Syndicate Established 131

The borrowing banks have decided to form a syndicate for the Yuping Railway loan, which will be established after the contract is signed. This syndicate will be attached to the Bank of China and will be managed by the Bank of China's general management office, without setting up a separate office like the Italian Gengzi Indemnity loan syndicate in order to save expenses.

Construction to Begin Soon 132

The German firm responsible for the materials for the construction of the Yuping Railway has sent personnel to Germany to order them. The first round of bidding for the contracting of the earthwork and stonework for the line and stations from Yushan to Nanchang for the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway has been scheduled for 2:00 PM on the 25th of this month at the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Bureau in Hangzhou. As for borrowing from the banks in Shanghai, it will be resolved after construction begins, so the signing of the contract is expected to happen soon.

German's Great Feat - Circumnavigating the Globe by Bicycle - Has Arrived in Shanghai from Guangzhou via Hankou - Will Follow the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway to Beijing 135

The Da Mei Evening News reports that a German named Mr. Liddig set off from his hometown of Treiden by bicycle in 1932 to circumnavigate the globe. He recently arrived in Hankou from Guangzhou and came to Shanghai by waterway, arriving in port last night. He has traveled 14,000 miles since he started. He plans to stay in Shanghai for eight days, then drive to Beijing via Hangzhou, and then go north to Tianjin, which he expects to reach in two weeks. Mr. Liddig has passed through Venice, Athens, Istanbul, Baghdad, and other places, and then entered India. In Calcutta, his bicycle was damaged, so he replaced it with a new one. After leaving Guangzhou on May 18th, he averaged 100 miles per day. On flat roads, he could travel 10 miles per hour, but near the border of Hunan, the roads were rugged and difficult to travel, and sometimes the person had to carry the bicycle. He finally arrived in Hankou on June 6th. After visiting Korea and Japan, Mr. Liddig plans to cross the Pacific to the United States and then drive across the Americas to reach the Atlantic coast.

Public Telephones Installed Inside Postal and Telegraph Offices 136

Employee of Livestock Plantation Company Sentenced for Enticing and Raping Farmer's Daughter 137

Jiang A'yu, a farmer in Jiangwan Township, has a daughter, named A'zeng, who is 19 years old this year and works in the fields at home. Although A'zeng was born into a farming family, she is very beautiful. Since Jiangwan has adopted the urban atmosphere of Shanghai, she also cut her hair short and wears fashionable clothes when she is not working. Those who do not know her would never think she is a rural woman from the fields, so she and her father think highly of themselves and are unwilling to marry a local man. Therefore, her marriage prospects have been vacant. However, she has reached the age of marriage, and she cannot help but feel sentimental in the moonlight. It happened that Gu Huang, an employee of the Livestock Plantation Company in that area, met her, was astonished by her beauty, and enticed her, leading to a secret pregnancy. Gu Huang took this opportunity to entice A'zeng to hide in Fahua, but unexpectedly, Chief Gu had a wife and had already given birth to a son. Therefore, A'zeng was four months pregnant, her belly was bulging, and it was difficult for her to see her father, and she was unwilling to be a concubine, so love turned to hatred. At this time, she turned around and sent a message to her father, who took his daughter out and sued Gu in court. After trial yesterday, the examining official ruled that Gu should compensate the Jiang father and daughter 300 yuan, and Gu was sentenced to six months in prison for enticement and rape.

Woman Commits Suicide Due to Poverty and Illness 138

Liu Si, a native of Suqian, at No. 12 Xiaohuayuan, Huining Road, Nanshi, has no occupation. Every day, he goes to the trees in the fields to collect birds and insects and sells them to birdkeepers in the city temple to make a living. There is only his old wife, Liu Zhang, who is already 50 years old, has no children, and few brothers. The two elderly people are extremely poor. Liu Zhang also suffers from illness. Recently, she has been suffering from joint pain, confined to bed, and unable to bear the pain. She also has no money for medical treatment, so she thought that instead of enduring this painful life, it would be better to die sooner. Therefore, she had long intended to commit suicide. At 7:00 AM yesterday, while her husband was selling insects in the city, she got up alone and hanged herself on the bedpost. When her husband returned at noon, he saw his old partner commit suicide and burst into loud cries. The police arrived after the patrolman was informed, clarified the cause, and reported it to the Second District Police Station, who transferred the order to the local bailiff Gu Xueyuan to report to the local court to request an inspection.

Seventeen people attended, including Luo Xitao, Zhang Yujin, Rong Guangren, Mao Jinbao, and Pan Zhenshan. The chairman, Xin Yuling, gave a report, followed by a discussion: (1) On the case of renting a venue to facilitate office work, it was resolved to temporarily use the barber's public building at Ximen Xieqiao as a temporary office, and to move to a suitable location when there are sufficient funds. (2) On Tang Huaxuan's resignation as secretary, it was resolved to hire Mr. Pan Yaoting as the association's secretary. (3) On the case of stipulating the personnel for each department, it was resolved to hire Ni Zhizhan, Zhu Zhanghong, Pan Dongchu, Zhu Lianliang, Zhao Ziyuan, and others to serve as officers in various departments. (4) On how to continue publishing the Rongguang Newspaper to facilitate the association's publicity, it was resolved that the association would subsidize the Rongguang Newspaper's publicity expenses by 80 yuan per month, and those responsible would solicit national product advertisements to make up for the economic shortfall. (5) On the case of inviting representatives to conduct East-Partner cooperation, it was resolved to publicly elect Luo Shantao, Mao Jinbao, Chen Sijiang, Rong Guangren, and Xin Yuling as representatives to the East-Partner cooperation meeting. The meeting adjourned at 8:00 PM.

Its meaning is not fully conveyed, but it is actually connected to the source and flow of Confucius's teachings. It is like the "Tao Te Ching" and "Zhuangzi" of Taoism, and the "Diamond Sutra" of Buddhism. Mr. Sun once said to someone, "The 'Analects', 'Mencius', 'The Great Learning', and 'The Doctrine of the Mean' are books for learning, with their beginnings and ends, their order of importance. They are doors to esoteric and exoteric, gradual and sudden teachings. The way to illustrate the relationship between heaven and man is the 'Doctrine of the Mean' as the most important." Weather Report 153

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the northeast of China and the surrounding areas of Shandong are cloudy, with winds from the south to the west. In the middle reaches of the Yangtze River and this area, there are occasional showers or drizzle, with winds from the southeast to the northeast, due to the eastward movement of the low pressure in Jiangxi. South of Ma'an Island, the sky is overcast and there are rain or fog in several places, with no directional wind. Also, within 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 80.4 and the lowest was 68.4. On the same day last year, the highest was 78.3 and the lowest was 68.4.

Special Feature: The Collapse of the National Economy: The Awakening of National Cooperative Production by Wu Tiecheng 丨Speech at the General Assembly of the Chinese Economic Credit Cooperative Mobilization Team on June 9th丨 154

Chairman and distinguished guests, I am attending the general assembly of the Economic Credit Cooperative Mobilization Team today, and I have a very good feeling seeing all of you present. This feeling is that a new force of people involved in social undertakings in Shanghai has emerged to participate. In the past, we often saw that those who were involved in social undertakings in Shanghai were always the same few people coming and going. But today, I have seen many new faces. Among them, there are many friends I know, but whether I know them or not, I believe that all of you present today are not participating because of personal relationships, but because you have a considerable understanding and interest in the Economic Credit Cooperative. From this, it can be seen that the number of people participating in social undertakings in Shanghai is increasing day by day. This is a very good phenomenon in Shanghai, and it is also something I, as a public servant of the locality, am grateful for regarding the future of Shanghai.

China, in the era of isolationism, was an agricultural economic era of self-cultivation and self-weaving. At that time, people's lives were very simple, and the living materials they needed were also very simple. What we needed, we could provide for ourselves, so at that time, there was no talk of a national economic life. For example, if we wanted to eat, we could cultivate it ourselves. If we wanted to wear clothes, we could spin yarn and weave cloth ourselves. Life was extremely simple at that time. However, since the Opium War, foreign cannons opened the door to China. Chinese politics suffered a blow, and because of this blow, changes occurred. This change has been continuing non-stop for the past eighty or ninety years, and the general life of the people has also undergone a great change due to this great influence, which is the revolution of life. However, in this nearly century-long tide of great change and great revolution, we have actually not established an economic organization that conforms to modern economic principles. Therefore, although China has been changing non-stop every day for the past century, the general public is still unaware and has not paid attention to the fluctuations of this era. The most obvious revolution in our lives can be seen in the cities. As long as we compare our lives in the cities with the lives of people in the countryside, we can know how much our lives have been affected by the fluctuations of this world trend. But when we think about it thoroughly, we are still behind the times. We have not moved forward in accordance with the trend of the times. As for our economic organization, it is still very simple. Most people do not have a recognition of modern economic organizations, so they cannot generate the effect of organization, and many new organizations and new plans often fail. This is such a pity.

Since we cannot return to the state of life a hundred or fifty years ago, and we cannot leave the city to live the lives of our ancestors in the countryside, we must plan for ourselves. If one person cannot plan, then many people should come together to plan. However, our general public only knows how to consume and is unwilling to produce. It's as if people want to ride in cars, but we ourselves don't know how to manufacture them. But the general public believes that we have plenty of money, so we can take the money to buy cars manufactured by others. If we want to wear suits, and the woolen products we produce ourselves are not good, we can buy imported goods. We don't care if our money is taken away by others, as long as we are beautiful and comfortable. These wishful thinking calculations are certainly very good for individuals, but the result of such wishful thinking calculations will lead our nation to its death. We don't need to look elsewhere, just look at Shanghai. People in Shanghai who used to be wealthy lived in three-story shikumen houses. Now, the wealth of the wealthy is actually not much more than those who used to live in three-story houses, or only slightly more. And they all want to go to the quiet areas of the Western District to live in very modern and complete Western-style houses. Everyone enjoys enjoyment, but one day, our money will be used up invisibly, and we will be deeply led to the death of our nation. Just now, Mr. Zhang Shouyong reported that our customs deficit last year reached as much as 700 million yuan. The only skill our ancestors passed down to us was farming, but now even the country's food supply cannot be self-sufficient and still relies on foreigners. Not to mention other cotton and woolen fabrics for clothing. China is known as a country that stands on agriculture, and the Chinese people's skill in farming is famous throughout the world. The farming methods of many rice-eating nations in the world are mostly taught to them by us. But now the rice that the Chinese eat has to be transported from foreign countries. How can this be allowed? As for the wheat that our compatriots in the north eat, most of it also has to rely on foreign imports, so that last year the import of agricultural products accounted for 250 million yuan of the total deficit of 700 million yuan. That is, the woolen and cotton fabrics that we wear also nearly reached 100 million yuan. Our ancestors never expected that there would be such unpromising descendants who enjoy themselves every day and do not know that we are now enjoying ourselves, and our descendants will have no chance to live in the future.

Therefore, we must not only plan for ourselves now, but also plan for our descendants. Our ancestors planned a lot for us. Three years ago, when we flew from Beijing to Nanjing and then to Hangzhou, passing through the wealthy areas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, we could see very clearly from the air. Such as the organization of the countryside, the rivers, fields, roads, etc., our ancestors had arranged everything for our descendants. We cannot take the industry left to us by our ancestors, as well as the survival skills taught to us, and promote them. We are truly unpromising. We must not harm our descendants. We must be able to carry on the past and open up the future, so that our descendants can survive generation after generation. If we only plan for ourselves now and not for our descendants, what will we give them in the future and teach them to inherit our cause? Therefore, we should not just enjoy ourselves now, not just plan for ourselves, but also plan for our descendants. Eighteen years ago, when I returned from Honolulu, I met an old American woman on the ship. She told me that I had been to China several times and had seen many Chinese students go to the United States to study medicine every year. After graduating and returning to China, they should plan for the public health of various places in China. However, the public health of various places in China is still as unhygienic as before. She also said that those Chinese who returned from studying medicine in the United States only knew how to keep the inside of their houses very clean, with all kinds of sanitary facilities and ditches, etc., very complete. But outside the house, they didn't care about anything. In this way, it is certainly good for one person to pay attention to hygiene, but what is the use of one person's hygiene? It is necessary to know that without paying attention to public health, one person's hygiene is useless. It's like the many poor people in Zhabei, whose food, clothing, and shelter are all very dirty and easily lead to epidemics. After an epidemic breaks out in the area, those of us who pay attention to hygiene will also be infected by them. Therefore, we must plan as a whole, not only for ourselves now, but also for our descendants in the future.

I remember the year before last, the National Women's Christian Association held a representative meeting in Shanghai, with hundreds of women representatives from all over the country, most of whom came from rural villages in the interior. One day, they invited me to give a speech. The first thing I told them was, I said, "Everyone, you have come to Shanghai this time to attend the National Women's Christian Association Representative Meeting. Most of you have never been to Shanghai before. Now that you have suddenly come to Shanghai and seen that the Shanghai market is so prosperous and the people's lives are so extravagant and romantic, you must not have the wrong ideas in your minds. You must know that Shanghai's current prosperity is not real prosperity, and the extravagant and romantic lives of those special classes of people in Shanghai are not the result of their genuine efforts and contributions to society and the country. Please recognize these two points clearly and do not have the wrong ideas. If you see this false prosperity in Shanghai and the extravagant lives that are not obtained by your own efforts and develop the wrong ideas, then you will inevitably make many mistakes when you go back to work in the interior in the future." This is what I said to the national women's youth representatives first. (See my book "The Revival of the Chinese Nation and the Women's Movement" published in major newspapers in Shanghai.) The Rotary Club once held a meeting and meal and invited me to give a speech. I boldly said to them, "Shanghai's prosperity is certainly what every citizen living in Shanghai hopes for. But Shanghai has already prospered to this point today. Our efforts in the future should not make Shanghai's prosperity become a deformed state. Our first step is to strive to maintain the current prosperity. Only by maintaining the current prosperity can we further prosper in the future. Because Shanghai's prosperity today is not the result of the efforts of Shanghai citizens in the past. In other words, the efforts of Shanghai citizens in the past should not have resulted in such prosperity today. Today's prosperity in Shanghai is very strange, and there are other reasons involved. We know that the prosperity of a city is due to the joint efforts of all the people in the city, regardless of whether they are in agriculture, industry, commerce, or education. But judging from the past efforts of Shanghai citizens, today's prosperity should not exist." That's why I said that Shanghai's prosperity is false. How can false prosperity last? Therefore, I once compared Shanghai to a fish. Fish cannot live without water. So, where is the water? The water is in the rural villages in the interior. Now that our rural villages are on the verge of bankruptcy, the water has dried up. If the water dries up, how can the fish live? Therefore, if we want Shanghai's prosperity, we must also take into account the revival of the rural villages in the interior and the maintenance of the livelihoods of the farmers. If we can maintain the livelihoods of the farmers and jointly revive the rural villages, then the source of water will not dry up, and the fish in Shanghai will be able to survive. This is what I said and cited at the Rotary Club. (See my book (1) "The Basic Principles of a Prosperous Greater Shanghai" published in major newspapers in Shanghai (2) "The Future of Shanghai" published in the New China Magazine supplement.) However, I am a local official and also a local public servant. At the same time, you are Shanghai citizens and also the masters of Shanghai. It seems that I should not have said these words about Shanghai's prosperity being false in front of the masters. However, I, as a public servant, should be responsible for doing my best to improve these pathological conditions in Shanghai. As the masters of Shanghai, you should also understand and not avoid treatment. Therefore, I am pointing out these pathological conditions today, hoping that everyone will help the government to improve them together.

In short, although our economic organization and the state of the people's lives have undergone great changes, our economic organization is still unable to adapt to modern needs. Without a modern economic organization, our lives cannot become modern lives. Now is the era of an industrial economy with division of labor and cooperation, and not an agricultural economic era where everyone is on their own. Now our livelihood problems cannot be solved by ourselves alone. We must combine everyone's strength to solve everyone's problems. If everyone's problems can be solved, then our individual little problems can also be solved. Based on the spirit of equality, mutual assistance, and mutual benefit, we can seek the common interests of each individual and realize group life. This is the purpose of your Economic Credit Cooperative and is also the conclusion I want to contribute to you today.

Finally, I am very happy to see so many new faces here today. I myself am a local official and also a person who likes to participate in social undertakings. Whenever there is any guest meeting or undertaking, even in the midst of my busy schedule, I am very willing to participate. Therefore, I am very happy that many new forces have joined social undertakings. I hope that every time I participate in social undertakings, the people I see are different every time, and that everyone in society is engaged in social undertakings. Only in this way can society have a solution and the country have a solution. This is a little bit of my shallow opinion that I am contributing to you today. (End) June 1934 in Shanghai.

Ministry of Education Convenes University Presidents for Discussions: Decides on Four Military Training Measures for the Summer, Starting on the 28th of this Month for a Period of Three Weeks, Students Not Participating in Military Training Will Have Credit Reductions and Will Not Graduate 155

(Nanjing, 22nd) The Ministry of Education convened university presidents on the 22nd for a meeting to discuss matters related to summer military training in various universities. It was decided that: (1) It will start on the 28th of this month; (2) The training location will be at the Central Military Academy in Nanjing and [location not specified]. (3) The training period will be three weeks; (4) Students who do not participate in military training according to regulations after the summer vacation will have credit reductions and will not be allowed to graduate.

Implementation of Three-Week Summer Military Training for High Schools and Above in This City; Failure in Academic Year Military Training Will Result in Non-Promotion; City Education Bureau Yesterday Forwarded Achievement Calculation Methods, etc. 157

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau yesterday instructed all private universities and middle schools in the city and the Shanghai Municipal National Military Commission, stating: "As per the instruction No. 734 of the Ministry of Education and Training Supervisory Board, it is hereby noted that military education in high schools and above shall implement three weeks of extremely strict military training during each summer vacation, and a plan has been formulated and implemented through general notification. However, in past years, specific instructions regarding training methods have not been provided, resulting in insignificant achievements. Based on past experiences, in order to ensure the effective implementation and successful achievement of future summer training, the summer training methods should be formulated in advance to facilitate implementation. Now, the interim measures for school summer training have been revised eleven times. In addition to separate orders, the interim measures are hereby issued, instructing immediate compliance by your subordinates. This order." Additionally, "As per the instruction No. 746 of the Ministry of Education and Training Supervisory Board, it is hereby noted that schools have methods for assessing students' academic performance in various subjects, serving as standards for promotion and graduation. Military education is a compulsory subject for high schools or schools equivalent to high schools and above, and the assessment of its performance should be regulated to establish standards and ensure uniformity. Now, the method for calculating military training performance (with examples) in ten articles has been formulated. In addition to separate orders, the formulated method for calculating military training performance is hereby issued, instructing immediate compliance. This order," etc., and attached the interim measures for school summer military training (Editor's note: the measures were published in this newspaper on June 10) and a copy of the military training performance calculation method. Upon receiving this, in addition to separate orders, a copy of the aforementioned measures is hereby attached, instructing the school to comply with this order. The measures are attached as follows:

Military Training Performance Calculation Method 158

1. The subjects for academic and practical examinations in each term should be implemented according to the progress stipulated in the school's military education program.

2. Scores of 80 or above are graded as A, 70 or above as B, 60 or above as C, and below 60 as failing.

3. Examination periods are conducted in terms of academic year, term, summer vacation, etc., and held in stages at appropriate times.

4. Students who fail military training in any academic year are not allowed to be promoted.

5. Students whose absences in a term exceed one-third of the total military training hours in that term (or one-sixth for absences without leave) are not allowed to take the term examination, unless on special leave.

6. Deductions for absences without leave, etc., in a term shall be handled according to the established practices of the school's academic affairs department.

7. The average score of military training at the end of the term for secondary and higher education students and the centralized training score for graduates (which may be waived before explicit implementation) will be used as the military training score.

8. The military training score for each term is determined by averaging the academic and practical scores. Practical subjects in grade A are examined at the end of each term, but the score must still be averaged with the temporary examination score. Grade B academic subjects are divided into two categories: excellence and diligence, each accounting for 50% of the total score. The excellence score is assessed during the examination, and the diligence score is determined at the end of the term based on the student's usual absences without leave, etc. (1) No points are deducted for absences due to special leave. (2) No points are deducted for absences due to sick or personal leave within two weeks. For each absence beyond that, one point is deducted. (3) Two points are deducted for each absence without leave.

9. This calculation method shall be ordered, promulgated, and implemented by the Ministry of Education of the Training Supervisory Board.

(Examples)

Academic Year (First academic year score: 67, Second academic year score: 75): Add them together and divide by the number of academic years to obtain the military training completion score.

Term (Average academic and practical score of temporary examination: 66,

Average academic and practical score of term examination: 72):

Add them together and divide by two to obtain the term score.

(First semester score: 69, Second semester score: 70, Summer centralized training score: 62): Add them together and divide by three to obtain the academic year score.

(Military training completion score: 71, Graduate centralized training score: 63): Add them together and divide by two to obtain the total military training score.

Central University in the Past Two Years 173

— Luo Jialun

National Central University underwent significant reorganization in the 21st year of the Republic of China (1932). I, Jialun, arrived at the school to take charge on September 5th of that year. Two academic years have passed in the blink of an eye. Fortunately, with the government's support and guidance, and the united efforts of the entire school to seek progress, we have achieved a state of relative stability and laid a rough foundation for enrichment and development. At the beginning of the second academic year, I said that in the past year, students not only had books to read but also studied diligently, and professors not only had books to teach but also taught conscientiously. Now, as the second academic year is about to end, I deeply feel that this academic year has continued the spirit of the first academic year and has only increased, not diminished. Building a perfect national university cannot be achieved in one leap. There are still many areas for improvement, but there are some things that can be reported about the situation in the past two years. Therefore, I will list them briefly for your wise instruction.

Newly Built Seed Room of the College of Agriculture, National Central University

1. Reorganization of Colleges and Departments: The school originally had eight colleges: Arts, Science, Law, Education, Engineering, Agriculture, Medicine, and Commerce. Later, the Executive Yuan decided to make the Colleges of Medicine and Commerce in Shanghai independent, leaving six colleges. Among them, the departments still needed reorganization. Therefore, after considering the resolutions of the Reorganization Committee, complex departments such as Education and Sociology were merged. Departments that were more relevant to the actual needs of the country, such as the Department of Chemical Engineering in the College of Engineering and the Departments of Horticulture and Sericulture in the College of Agriculture, were restored. As a result of the reorganization, there are still six colleges and three departments. The College of Arts has five departments: Chinese Literature, Foreign Literature, Philosophy, History, and Sociology. The College of Science has six departments: Mathematics, Physics, Chemistry, Geology, Geography, and Biology. The College of Law has three departments: Law, Political Science, and Economics. The College of Education has two departments: Education and Psychology, and three divisions: Arts, Physical Education, and Health Education. The College of Engineering has five departments: Civil Engineering, Mechanical Engineering, Electrical Engineering, Architectural Engineering, and Chemical Engineering. The College of Agriculture has six departments: Agronomy, Forestry, Animal Husbandry and Veterinary Medicine, Agricultural Chemistry, Horticulture, and Sericulture.

2. Reorganization of Curriculum: University curricula in our country often have a large number of subjects and lack organic organization. Therefore, each college and department of the school separately redefined its educational goals and reorganized its curriculum, so that required and elective courses have clear regulations and are not subject to change due to individuals or circumstances. Once the core of the curriculum is formed, the meaning of teaching can be clarified. Fortunately, with the efforts and assistance of the deans, department heads, and professors, this work was largely completed after a long period of discussion lasting a year.

3. Focusing on Scholars and Emphasizing Full-Time Positions: Academics are inherently a specialized undertaking, and professors should devote themselves wholeheartedly. The school has suffered from years of turmoil and often feels empty. At the beginning of the reorganization, we made great efforts to retain good professors and recruited specialized scholars at any time. We asked those who could be full-time to be full-time. Taking this academic year as an example, a total of 76 professors were hired for the six colleges, of which 41 were full-time and 35 were part-time. In terms of the total number of courses taught, part-time professors teach only one-quarter of the courses taught by full-time professors. Most of the original professors who were retained were also full-time. I will not list them all here. Currently, most of the part-time professors are experts in certain specialized sciences, who are valued by the government and other academic institutions. We wanted to recruit them, but it was impossible in reality. We are deeply grateful for their assistance to the school.

4. Increasing Buildings and Equipment: To understand the difficulty of increasing buildings and equipment at the school, one must understand the school's financial situation. Before the 19th year of the Republic of China (1930), the school's budget was 2.04 million yuan. In the 20th year (1931), it was 1.92 million yuan (both including the expenses of the Colleges of Medicine and Commerce, but in the 20th year, there was a slight deduction due to the national crisis). In the 21st year (1932), the budget was still 1.92 million yuan. Later, due to the independence of the Colleges of Medicine and Commerce, in addition to the original expenses being split off, the school headquarters also allocated an additional 24,000 yuan per year for subsidies. As a result, the school's funding was reduced to 1.61 million yuan per year, with an actual receipt of 134,160 yuan per month from the Ministry of Finance. However, during these 21 months, there are also some noteworthy things about the construction and equipment. These are divided into two parts:

A. Construction: School construction is mostly related to academic undertakings. Some people think that since the school site is planned to be moved to the suburbs, why bother adding buildings to the original site? Little do they know that the construction of the new school buildings will take at least two or three years to complete from the current planning stage. From the autumn of the 21st year (1932) to the completion of the new school buildings, it will take a total of four or five years. During these four or five years, the school's academic progress cannot be conservative or stagnant. Moreover, saving money from the regular expenses to carry out construction has not received any special subsidies from the state, which is something that academic people are willing to see. 1. Adding a Library: 221,015 yuan (including steel bookshelves worth 55,500 yuan). The original library, reading room, and book storage capacity of the school were too small. The new library has two large reading rooms, accommodating 560 people, and five branch reading rooms, accommodating 200 people, plus a combined newspaper reading room and existing branch libraries, with a total capacity of over 1,000 people, which is about four times larger than before. The book storage capacity is one and a half times larger than before.

2. Building a New Music Classroom: 10,479 yuan. This was rebuilt from Mei'an and is used by the music group of the Department of Arts.

3. Building a New Seed Room for the College of Agriculture: 17,266 yuan. The College of Agriculture has collected tens of thousands of varieties of various species. Without specialized buildings for storage, research is impossible.

4. Building a New Greenhouse with Equipment for the College of Agriculture: 9,538 yuan. This is necessary for the research of the Departments of Agronomy and Horticulture.

5. Building a New Classroom for the College of Agriculture: The Entomology Research Room, 9,785 yuan.

6. Building Houses for the Department of Agricultural Chemistry, Department of Forestry, Department of Sericulture, and Agricultural Products Manufacturing Plant of the College of Agriculture, and Various Farm Buildings: 18,378 yuan.

Newly Built Music Room of National Central University

7. Building a New School Gate: 5,355 yuan. The old school gate was demolished during the National Assembly. Because it was related to the appearance of the entire school, it had to be rebuilt.

8. Building a New Science Classroom for the Experimental School: 23,100 yuan.

9. Renovating the Biology Building: 13,700 yuan. The original Biology Building was too bad, severely damaged, and the basement had 23 feet of accumulated water. It had to be thoroughly renovated.

10. Adding New Classrooms, Factories, and a Soap Factory to the College of Engineering: 6,790 yuan.

11. Renovating and Adding Classrooms and Laboratories to the College of Education (Nanjing Higher Normal School): 14,530 yuan. This is the oldest building in the school and must be thoroughly renovated. However, the clock tower was not repaired due to concerns about involving other departments.

12. Renovating the College of Law (Southeast Gate): 7,700 yuan.

13. Renovating the Teaching Staff Quarters: 5,785 yuan. This is also one of the earliest buildings in the school, dilapidated and in need of repair.

14. Renovating the New Student Dormitory: 4,739 yuan. Although this building was built in the 18th year of the Republic of China (1929), the foundation and materials were very bad and had to be repaired.

This is just a list of the larger and more expensive items, which amounts to 368,160 yuan. There are other smaller buildings and construction projects that cannot be listed one by one, totaling approximately 66,849 yuan. As for the payment of the completed auditorium and the purchase of seating, 14,455 yuan has also been paid. Therefore, the total amount paid for construction in these two years is 449,464 yuan. In addition, there are two new student dormitories under construction, with a contract price of 70,000 yuan, which are expected to be completed by the end of August. After completion, the student dormitories can be reorganized, which will greatly benefit the academic atmosphere. This money is taken from the deposit and rent of the original leased dormitory and is not included here for the time being. All major construction projects are overseen by the Engineering Committee, which is composed of professors, to ensure public decision-making and perfection.
