Spring and Autumn

The Scented Mists of the Imperial Incense 182

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

Of course, no matter how good the Empress Dowager's appetite was, she would never eat all of them at once, not even taste them all! On average, she tasted no more than three or four dishes per meal. The rest were either discarded or taken by the female officials, palace maids, and upper-level eunuchs in turn.

The Empress Dowager always sat alone and enjoyed her meals alone. However, sometimes she would teach me to accompany her. But I could only eat standing, not sitting like her. Her dining table was not a whole table. In fact, there could not be such a large table that could hold a full hundred bowls of dishes. Even if there was, it would be too clumsy, and the Empress Dowager would never like it! So we had a set of small tables prepared, and when they were put together temporarily, they were just enough to hold the hundred main dishes. Although the table problem was solved in this way! However, the dishes were really too far away from the Empress Dowager. Apart from the few dishes close to her, she could not reach them with her chopsticks and spoon. Then, did the Empress Dowager really have to look at these dishes but not be able to reach them? No, no, readers do not need to worry about her. It turns out that there was a eunuch next to her who was specially serving the Empress Dowager! This eunuch's name was Zhang De. After the Empress Dowager Cixi passed away, this person succeeded Li Lianying as the chief eunuch in the Qing Palace. If the Empress Dowager liked a certain dish and wanted to try it, she would order Zhang De to respectfully bring it closer and ask the Empress Dowager to take a bite. However, this errand of serving dishes was really not easy. Every hand gesture and every step had to be very solemn. After the Empress Dowager finished her meal, all the dishes would be taken away and we could eat them freely. Ninety percent of them were still completely intact, like sacrificial dishes taken down when worshiping ancestors. (65)

Short Biography of San Yu 183

— Shi Jiu

San Yu was a school worker in a certain middle school in Zhejiang. We were colleagues for two years. The so-called "colleagues" is not intended to be respectful, because school workers are also the main figures in the school and should be in an equal position with the principal, faculty, staff and students.

San Yu had a strong body, iron-like wrists, and a pair of hairy legs. He was in charge of the "comprador" in the school and never failed. The school was located in a remote seaside area, about seven or eight miles away from the nearest bustling town. In order to send correspondence to the post office and purchase various supplies, it was natural that the school had to select a suitable person to serve as this "comprador". San Yu went in the morning and returned at noon; he had to go out again in the afternoon and returned at dusk. Therefore, the distance he traveled every day was always more than thirty miles, and he braved the wind and rain, without interruption in the cold and heat.

Although he was illiterate, he never made mistakes. If you asked him to bring something, as long as you explained it to him, he would handle it to your satisfaction. Sometimes he felt that a certain item was expensive and would discuss it with us, so that we would not suffer a loss. Sometimes he accidentally returned one copper plate less, and I had already forgotten it, but he would still find it and return it, refusing to grease his palms.

Whenever he carried a heavy load on a pole, shouting "Hang Yu, Hang Yu," and walked into the school gate, everyone in the school would see him and say, "San Yu. Are you back?"

One summer, I took a steamer back to my hometown. When the steamer was about to set sail, San Yu gave me two packs of snacks for the road and said "Bon voyage" before leaving. I still remember it today. Although these snacks were very coarse, his kindness was truly appreciated.

"If you lose the rites, seek them in the wild." We all called San Yu honest and took a photo with him to keep as a souvenir.

After Returning to Shanghai 184

— Qiu Hong

After six years of being away from Shanghai, fate finally drove me to see it again. Some of my friends have hung up their lawyer's signs; some have hung up their accountant's signs; and even a few are going in and out of cars and living in foreign houses. However, there are also a few who are unfortunately living a hard life; they are almost short of food and clothing, and they have a home but cannot return. Because the environment has changed, everything is somewhat different from before, but I have not changed the habit of taking two newspapers in and out of the office every morning and evening.

Before returning to Shanghai, in my hometown, I was very worried about Shanghai. After coming, I felt that it was nothing special, not worth mentioning. After being caged in a very tall house with teak floors for nine hours every day, when the sun sets, I have to move my body to the wide road and walk around. I took the newspaper and ran to the bustling and crowded places, wanting to grab some of the impressions that Shanghai gave me six years ago. But I was finally disappointed. Shanghai, which has progressed very quickly, is very different from before: many houses have been rebuilt, the neon lights shine everywhere, and even the street hawkers are not the same batch as before.

Stepping into the playground, dance hall, or song and dance, is also something that did not exist before. There are more stalls selling 15% discount books, the display of scientific psychic diagrams, and the decoration of Oriental toys. Although there are those who file lawsuits and ask for copper coins, as before, the only one I recognize is the female beggar with some pockmarks on her face and blurred eyes. Her thin, yellow face is still the same as before, and there does not seem to be a trace of change. Perhaps because her eyes are blurred and she cannot see all the changes, she herself has not changed for me to see. I often see her, often think this way, and often forget to give her a copper coin.

When I walk back from the road or come out of the playground, passing in front of the dance hall or the big theater, there are often pairs of young men and women crowding into the car, with slight smiles on their faces. Time steals away in the laughter I see every night. Counting on my fingers, it has been two months since I returned to Shanghai, and a layer of black light has been added to the front of a light blue long shirt from carrying newspapers.

Chen Taoist 185

— Tong Chu

Who knows that a madman is particularly popular, and his business is particularly prosperous. When people have incurable diseases, they excitedly shout: "We must invite Chen Taoist to perform a ritual, chant a few scriptures, or we won't be able to hold on!"

Generally, people only know that his surname is Chen, and no one knows his name; because he exorcises ghosts and demons for sick families, "Chen Taoist" has become his great name. He is a popular person in my hometown, everyone respects him, loves him, and everyone has a warning in their heart: "If I get sick, he is the only one who can save me."

The reason why he became famous is well-known. One summer, Wang Yuanqiao's son suffered a strange illness. The doctors all refused, and the witches said ghosts and monsters, said gods and Tao, said that Yama could only save his son and no other method would work. At this time, Chen Taoist volunteered and said loudly: "As long as I chant a scripture, the illness will turn around immediately." Everyone knew that he was a madman, so how could Yuanqiao believe him. Later, in vague hopes, he allowed him to try. Strangely enough! The illness did turn around and gradually got better.

"Ah, Chen Taoist has great skills! I'm afraid he is a star sent down by Zhang Tianshi!"

Chen Taoist's hands are always trembling. When walking, he walks with bowlegs, and raises his arms, staggering, looking like he is dozing off from a distance. He has never spoken a clear sentence. Saliva often hangs from the corner of his mouth, especially when eating or standing and looking at women, but women do not avoid him because of this, but instead give him a flirty look, and everyone laughs: "Ah! That Chen Taoist!"

Short Story

Yellow Dusk by the Bridge 186

— A Ping

Holding hands, with hearts aligned, like a following shot in a movie, they walked along this quiet path, treading on the fragmented shadows of the trees. The early summer breeze caressed their hair and light clothing, while also causing the shadows on the ground to sway. Silently, they occasionally exchanged glances and smiled. They cherished this precious meeting, but neither wanted to pour out the words long held in their hearts. In the exchange of glances, they seemed to understand each other more clearly than with words.

Their footsteps gradually slowed. She glanced at him, and he smiled, readjusted his pace, and walked forward. "We've reached the new bridge. Isn't it getting late?" She gazed at the bridge's reflection on the river, illuminated by the setting sun, reminding him as if speaking to herself.

"Let's watch the sunset. We can take a car back later."

They continued to walk forward, stepping on the shadows of the trees on the path.

They arrived at the bridge. They sat side-by-side on the stone railing, their gazes cast far into the distance, as if appreciating the afterglow of the setting sun, wasting one minute, two minutes, five minutes.

"Isn't it getting late? What about all the things you wanted to say?" She stood up, smoothed out the wrinkles in her clothes, and asked with a seemingly natural smile.

"There are really too many things. I don't know where to begin."

"Then speak. It's getting late!"

"Actually, isn't it better not to say anything?"

"Yes, I understand what you mean, but life is too dull!"

He turned his head and gazed at her tearful face. She looked away. "X, that doesn't sound like something a child would say?" He suddenly grabbed her arms.

"Do you still think I'm a child?" Her head lowered, and she sobbed.

"Quick, don't be like this, X," he lifted her head and said, "Listen to me. You're still young. Don't let your environment misguide your life. Besides, a child shouldn't be so pessimistic!"

"I understand what you mean." She nodded slightly, a crystalline teardrop rolling from the corner of her pursed lips onto his knee.

"Let's go back. It's really getting late." (The sun had completely sunk into the heart of the river.) He helped her up and said softly near her temples, "You have to listen to me. It was wrong of me to hurt you by not writing. Think about happy things. You haven't reached the age where life is too dull."

"You still treat me like a child!" Tears welled up in her eyes, and her lower lip trembled.

"Don't misunderstand me! I'm not saying a child who doesn't understand 'life,' but that you don't need to understand the reasoning of 'life is too dull,' right? We're both young!"

Slowly, they walked back along the path. The early summer breeze caressed their hair and clothing. Gentle footsteps glided by, leaving behind a blur of tree shadows on the path. Gradually, the two figures disappeared into the whisper of the dusk.

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 187

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 30: Watching Grieving Wild Geese, Guarding the Homeland with Heads Bowed; Bullet Piercing Strong Arm, Blood Staining the Lonely City

Just as there was a shot near the first trench, Yin Deren moved the rifle bolt and fired dozens of shots in that direction. Following this gunfire, there was a response from the other side, shooting directly at where Yin Deren was standing. Yin Deren shouted, "One thousand meters, fire!" The brothers followed his command and fired their guns. However, Yin Deren felt a sense of depression and discomfort from being transferred in from outside the fort. At this moment, with the firing, he felt that only by killing more people could he feel relieved. Therefore, he moved the machine gun, half-crouched, not running at the embankment opening, but only aiming at the area with the most enemy gunfire, and fired from the embankment opening. He sometimes went from east to west, and sometimes from west back to east, like a madman, shouting, "Brothers, hold your breath, see the enemy clearly and fire!" As he shouted, the enemy's small bronze cannon began to bombard the city embankment. A shell hit, blowing away two or three sections of the embankment opening. Yin Deren became even more anxious and placed the machine gun on the side of the gap, firing a burst. The enemy was preparing to rush over from here, and were met with this burst of fire, causing many to fall. He forgot himself and waved his right hand in the air, saying, "Little ones, come on!" Just at this moment, he felt half of his body go numb, and he was hit in the arm. Immediately, his hands became somewhat unresponsive. Only then did he lean against the embankment wall and sit down, holding the wound on his right arm with his left hand. When he touched his arm, he felt that his palm was sticky, and he was bleeding a lot. It seemed that the bullet had passed through his arm. However, he did not let the brothers know, and continued to shout, "One thousand five hundred meters, fire!" Then he lifted a corner of his clothes, held it in his mouth, pulled out his bayonet, and cut off a long piece of the hem. He used it as a bandage, slightly bent his arm, bit one end of the cloth, and with his left hand holding the cloth, wrapped it tightly around the wound on his arm, first stopping the bleeding, and then calming down. Shen Bao Radio Weekly

Concerning the "Radio Treasure Detector" 188

— Zhu Yunjun

On the ninth of this month, this publication carried an article on the "Radio Treasure Detector." I had done this myself in the winter before last, because the Radio Craft June 1932 magazine had a very detailed explanation, and its principle was feasible, so I spent more than sixty yuan at that time to buy light bulbs and other parts. After assembling it according to the instructions, the effectiveness of the two devices was still good, so I installed them in my family's ancestral hall in the inland, with the angle adjusted. Another person buried iron objects in an oil can underground, about two feet deep, in advance. Then I used this device to search. First, I held the device high, two or three feet above the ground, and sure enough, there was no sound. When I placed it about one foot above the ground, a sharp sound suddenly arose, deafening. I thought the experiment was a success and was very happy, but when I dug it up, there was nothing. I felt very strange. Later, I tested it on various ground surfaces and it could make a sound in the same way, completely indistinguishable. Only then did I realize that it had failed. But there is one point: whether it is because the device is too sensitive, or because the soil is too damp, I have not yet thoroughly researched. However, in this time of economic decline, I am afraid that someone will rashly experiment. It will end up with "trying to steal a chicken but losing the rice." So I wrote down what I have learned from my experience for everyone's reference. (No payment)

Coordination Method of Remote-Control Sound Transmission Line 189

— Yizhi

Broadcast stations, public lecture halls, and theaters often separate the sound receiving point from the sound output point, using a transmission line to transport the received sound waves to another location. After being amplified by an amplifier, the sound is output. This type of device is called the remote-control transmission method. This method, in addition to avoiding interference between sound receiving and sound output, allows the sound receiving room and the sound output room to be set up in appropriate locations. For example, due to the location of the antenna, broadcast stations cannot be located in bustling urban areas, which is inconvenient for broadcasters to travel to and from. Therefore, it is advisable to place the sound receiving room in a location with convenient transportation, and the received sound waves are then input to the broadcasting station via a transmission line. However, when sound waves are transmitted, because the transmission line is very long, there is inductance and capacitance between the two lines. Therefore, if directly connected to the amplification stage, in addition to the sound quality and volume being greatly inferior to the original source, there will also be problems such as tremolo and noise. The solution is to add appropriate coordination to the transmission line before connecting it to the amplification stage.

Diagram 1 shows the coordination method of a remote-control sound transmission red line. T1 is a transmission line transformer, T2 is a microphone transformer, R1 is a 226-ohm resistor, R2 is a 74-ohm resistor, and R3 is a 67-ohm resistor. The characteristic impedance between the transmission lines is 500 ohms. A shield should be used between the transmission transformer and the microphone transformer, and the transmission line should also be shielded with a lead pipe to eliminate static electricity and other interference. The sound source is input to the T1 transformer from a microphone or pickup, and then transmitted to another location via the transmission line. After being matched by an H-shaped resistance balancer, it goes directly to the first stage of the T2 microphone transformer and the amplifier. This method has been used by several broadcasting stations and public lecture halls in the United States, as well as amateur radio stations, and the results are said to be very good. I am introducing it here for reference.

A Two-Tube Radio That Does Not Need A Transformer For AC or DC Power 190

— Qi

An excellent and perfect radio does not only rely on strong power and complex circuitry. Even an ordinary small-scale radio, if designed carefully and manufactured legally, can still achieve amazing results. Recently, a type of transformerless radio sold on the market has been quite popular among the general public, likely because of its exquisite manufacturing and low price.

Recently, in my spare time, I tried to make a two-tube transformerless radio, using a new-style 25Z5 as a half-wave rectifier (so it can be used for both AC and DC), and an E138 pentode car tube for detection. The amazing effectiveness is not inferior to 47 or 2A5, etc. And this machine is economical, simple, beautiful, and compact, which is superior to those using transformers, and DC power can also be used, so it is quite suitable for use in the mainland with DC power plants. Based on the above advantages, this small-power radio can be made

, to achieve a perfect state. Amateur enthusiasts, why not give it a try? The circuit diagram is published below:

The coil used in this machine, in order to make it take up less space, needs to be wound on a plastic tube. L can be wound with 30 gauge wire for fifteen turns on a plastic tube with a radius of one and a half inches, with a spacing of about two-tenths of an inch. Then use the same gauge wire to wind L1 eighty turns. L2 can be wound on a one-inch diameter tube for about forty turns. When installing, if you can arrange it compactly, you can put it in a small box to make a pocket radio, which is also possible. Also, because the sensitivity is quite high, if it is used as a travel radio and does not use a sky or earth line, according to the test, you can also receive very clear music. Finally, it is important to note that the primary coil L cannot be connected to the secondary coil L1, otherwise it will easily cause danger. In addition, the capacities of other components are noted in detail on the diagram, so there is no need to repeat them.

Wiring Summary 191

— Jiang Zhiban

The wiring method of a radio receiver seems simple at first, but its importance is no less than the quality of the circuit and components. When beginners make their own radios, they often overlook this point, and the results are often not good, and even damage the components. All amateur researchers should pay attention to this.

(1) Component Arrangement: The first step in wiring is

arranging components. Proper arrangement saves space, shortens wiring, avoids useless inductive effects, and maximizes the effectiveness of the radio. The key points of the arrangement, in terms of DC radios, for the sake of economy, if metal chassis panels and shields are not used, it is best to have a wider space. It is best to arrange the lamp sockets in a single row, with the filaments facing the panel, which can shorten the wiring a lot. The audio frequency transformer can be placed between the two lamp sockets. If there are more than two, they should be arranged at right angles and should be far away from the tuning coil. It is best to also be at right angles. The radio frequency amplification tube should be far away from the detection tube, and its tuning coil should be far away from the one used in the detection stage and at right angles. As for AC machines, the above points should also be noted. However, AC machines often use metal isolation, and complex

use multiple bypass capacitors and chokes. Therefore, although the arrangement is small, inductive effects can be avoided. However, power transformers and filters should all be far away from radio frequency or intermediate frequency circuits. The shield used for the coil should be twice the diameter of the coil. The distance between the coil and the bottom plate and the top of the shield is one inch each. Otherwise, the effectiveness will be poor. At the same time, attention should also be paid to the arrangement of easily heated parts, such as rectifier tubes, high-power output tubes, and power transformers. Be sure to dissipate heat quickly and avoid damaging other components. This is the general idea of component arrangement.

(2) Wiring Procedures: (A) All wiring must be well insulated. Bare wires can only be used in very simple circuits. The commonly used conductors are preferably 18 gauge varnished yarn covered. In high-end shortwave machines, 14 gauge varnished yarn covered is mostly used. Since the filament current of AC machines is quite large, very thick stranded wires must be used to connect the filaments. The wiring of the tetrode copper cap should also use thick and reliable insulation, because it is often pulled and easily damaged. (B) The DC machine wiring should be neat. The bends of the wire should be at right angles, and the varnish coating on the wire should not be damaged. The method is to use a piece of foreign paper to pad in the needle-nosed pliers and bend it. All wire joints should be bent into question mark (?) shapes and tightly screwed onto the screws. It is best not to use pliers for the screw caps, but to use a screw cap socket to turn them to avoid damage. (C) AC machine wiring should be straightforward, so it is intricate and complex. The wires often touch each other, and the voltage is high, so attention must be paid to the insulation of the wires. DC machines are best to be soldered, while AC machines must be soldered, because components such as fixed resistors and fixed capacitors, etc.

If not soldered, there is no way to make them contact firmly. (D) Wiring should be orderly and step by step to avoid errors. The general wiring method is to first connect the filaments, then the screen circuit. Grid circuit, screen grid circuit, sky and earth line circuit. Those with less experience should use a graded wiring method. First, follow the above order to install the detection stage, and try listening to be satisfied, and then add the audio frequency amplification stage, and then try listening to be satisfied, and finally add radio frequency amplification. If it is installed like this, it is easiest to succeed. (E) It is best to use five-color wires for wiring, which is not only beautiful, but also easy to check and not easy to make mistakes. It is also a necessary condition for a high-end radio. For one application, the filament uses black (一), the screen circuit uses red, to indicate high voltage. The grid circuit uses yellow. The screen grid circuit uses green. (3) Small Key Points: The following key points must not be ignored, otherwise, the result will disappoint you. (A) Before installing the components, check them carefully. (B) For all components that should be insulated from the metal plate, ensure that the degree of insulation is very reliable. (C) When installing a variable capacitor, first fully rotate the movable plate to avoid damage. (D) For fixed resistors and tubular capacitors used in AC machines, it is best to first roughly assemble several related ones. Use a small square of thick paper that has been boiled in wax to connect them to each other on both sides of the paper, so that the wiring is short, the space is small, and it will not be messy and twisted. This type of connection is used in all imported products. (E) The wires used for wiring must be matched in length, bent, and cut. It is better to be slightly longer than too short, too short is a waste. (F) The grid circuit and screen circuit wiring of DC machines should not be close or parallel, otherwise inductive effects will easily occur.

In short, the wiring work is very important, and even small details should not be ignored. Only then can there be achievements. Amateur researchers should pay attention to this!

American Radio Corporation Big Sale: Steward Company at 362 Nanjing Road, 386 Gongguan Road, 162 Hubei Road, and Steward's three branch companies at 316 East Broadway are simultaneously holding special big sales. The radio repair department of Yada Company at 24 Nanjing Road has recently become more crowded with repair work. Free Talk

About Mass Language 193

— Hu Yuzhi

In our society, a certain social stratum that has been in a dominant position for thousands of years is visibly declining rapidly. Following the decline of this social stratum, all cultures that represent this social stratum—philosophy, morality, education, law, love, literature, and art—are also in the process of decline. The language representing the consciousness of this social stratum is naturally no exception.

If the May Fourth Movement did not make much contribution in other aspects, at least in the language revolution, it has already knocked down the dominant class's camp to a scattered mess. Although the leaders of the May Fourth Literary Revolution did not clearly recognize the social mission, they, on the one hand, actually sentenced "Classical Chinese" to death, unconsciously disarming the words of the dominant class. On the other hand, due to the large amount of practical application of "Vernacular Chinese," literature is no longer a forbidden place for the public. Therefore, for the decline of the dominant class's language and the generation of mass language, the May Fourth Movement did play a considerable role in promotion.

But this declining social stratum is definitely not willing to decline without any resistance. The language representing this social stratum, like all the cultures representing this social stratum, will inevitably resurrect from the ashes when it reaches a considerable time. Moreover, the May Fourth Literary Revolution originally did not do it thoroughly. It only opposed "Classical Chinese" and "Vernacular Chinese," and did a little bit of work on the point that literature approaches spoken language, but lightly let go of the main root of the Chinese character—representing ancient feudal consciousness—and at the same time lacked effort in the construction of the new mass language. Therefore, it left a way out for this old Chinese language that was sentenced to death in secret.

Sure enough, at present, following the political and social restoration tendency, the ghosts of the old Chinese language have reappeared. These ghosts show up in four different forms: the first kind maintains its original face, which is the so-called "Classical Chinese Revival" movement recently. The second kind is wearing the coat of "Vernacular Chinese" to return from the dead. (For example, the articles of the Saturday School and Zhang Henshui's novels all use the form of "Vernacular Chinese" to express the consciousness of the declining social stratum.) The third kind is mixed in the middle of "Vernacular Chinese," such as many popular works, inevitably reveal the fox tail of the declining language in form and consciousness from time to time. (Mr. Le Sibing is the most loyal to "Vernacular." But unfortunately, an article of less than a thousand words by Mr. Le published in yesterday's Free Talk has two classics: "The bell ringer automatically untied the bell, since Zeng below::" This is just an example. Mr. Le is like this, and "since Zeng below" naturally goes without saying. It can be seen that dead words are doing tricks everywhere.) The fourth kind is appearing wearing the masks of "style," "spirit," and "quotation style." Although this kind of ghost is the most well-behaved, its main function is to tend to the restoration of the language, which is very obvious.

These four kinds of ghosts, united together, are superficially terrible. But in practice, these are just the struggles of the declining language before and after. No matter how they struggle, they cannot save the fate of decline, because the social stratum using this language tool is declining, and the consciousness of this social stratum is also declining every day. Therefore, despite advocating "Classical Chinese" in education, the consciousness contained in "Classical Chinese" is eliminated, and the higher the "Classical Chinese," the more incomprehensible it becomes. As for the Saturday School's return from the dead, it does not have much impact after all. Those who advocate spiritual literature or quotation styles will eventually reveal their original shape.

Healthy people are not afraid of ghosts. The declining language of the declining class will not have much future. The main issue lying in front of us is not to oppose "Classical Chinese" or "quotation style," etc., but to actively improve the construction of mass language tools and build language for mass application that represents mass consciousness.

Therefore, I feel that the mass language proposed by Mr. Chen Zizhan and Chen Wangdao has an important meaning. However, I have some opinions here that are not completely consistent with the two Mr. Chens. I think:

(1) "Mass language" should be interpreted as "language representing mass consciousness." The difference between "mass language" and "Vernacular Chinese" in the May Fourth era is that "Vernacular Chinese" does not necessarily represent mass consciousness. And mass language must not allow the declining social consciousness to enter the city gate.

(2) "Mass language" must be close to spoken language. But the absolute "unity of writing and speech" should be when the organization of speech has made considerable progress.

(3) The ideal tool for Chinese language to become universally used must be to abandon hieroglyphs and become

phonetic characters. Therefore, at present, writing words together, stroke-reducing characters, and Mandarin phonetics are all worth promoting, because this is a step towards promoting the phoneticization and massification of Chinese language.

Thoughts After a Business College Performance (Part 2) 194

— By Wei

Is such a script really worth our Chinese youth, living in these turbulent times, spending so much effort rehearsing and performing, to realize the beauty of this script's stage techniques? How is it different from wasting time, like women who are idle and have nothing to do, perming their hair, wearing high heels, dragging long cheongsams on the ground, making them walk with swaying waists and showing off their swaying buttocks?

Of course, it also shows the cruelty of war. But, I think it says too little on this point.

As for this performance, the first thing I want to say is: I admire the spirit of the Business College students! It is admirable to perform such a heavy three-act play with only four people. Their hard work and effort are worth admiring.

Ms. Hu Mingxian, who played Zhenle, performed the best. As soon as she appeared on stage, her demeanor, actions, spirit, and facial expressions attracted me like a magnet, making me happy and tense. She played the role of a leisurely, calm, and gentle young woman very well, with a good, clever tone, especially her expressive eyes. It's just that her walking was not very natural, and later she did not perform as well as at the beginning. Originally, the role she played was very difficult to please, but she played it so movingly, which shows her talent for performance. Mr. Man Qiqiang, who played the father, had bright, expressive eyes and mouth, and was very capable of acting. He played the old father Maifu very hard. Mr. Zhou Huaijiu, who played Antre, did not do enough in many places. For example, when he first appeared on stage and saw his beloved wife after four years of separation, how ecstatic and nervous should he have been? But he didn't do it. He didn't reach the above-average level in any place that required tenderness, tension, depth, passion, or boredom. Only in the fierce places and the husband's attitude did he perform decently. Finally, I want to talk about Ms. Shi Jiyun, who played the heroine. This performance could not be as lively and vivid as the script, and subtly displayed to the audience. I think Ms. Shi's inability to perform is largely to blame. She can only smile. She can pass in expressing happy places, she can barely express simple places, but she simply cannot express sad places. She does not have the passion of a tragic protagonist. She does not feel how much passion a tragic protagonist needs to handle tragic plots, how much grandeur is needed to portray tragic emotions, and how much surging emotions are needed to convey the godlike expression that makes the audience both cry and laugh. In short, she is not a talent for acting in tragedies, and even the natural and lively places are not enough, and many gentle and charming places are also ignored. At first, when Antre returned home, she did not embrace him ecstatically, nervously, and passionately; she failed to throw herself into his arms several times; and her loud crying was also unnatural. When she read the letter from the American officer asking her to leave with him at the end of the second act, she had no expressions of surprise, secret joy, or sadness, which was also a big failure. Before the end of the third act, Le Langshi's performance of walking from the closet to the stove in despair was also unnatural. When she swayed to Antre and cried out, "Ah, this room, this stove, these things that we are used to: Ah, Antre!" At this time, how heartbroken and desperate should her expression be, crying madly and then laughing madly, with her voice and body trembling? Only in this way can she move people. However, the director did not grasp these important key points, so she did not achieve these things. It's a pity!

In short, the director did not ask the actors to show their courage in the tense parts of the whole play. In short, this public performance was generally acceptable, and the actors are all promising, as long as they are willing to work hard.

The stage lighting was not good, and the third act was too dark.

There were also omissions in the costumes. In such a winter, Zhenle was wearing a yellow gauze dress, and when Le Langshi's friends came, they were always wearing that thin single coat, and always wearing white shoes. Since they cried bitterly several times, they didn't even take out a handkerchief. These are small details that should also be noted. Some of the dialogues are in classical Chinese, dialects, and sentences that are not suitable for the stage. This is because of the translator's writing, and some of the terms are not dramatic. But the actors and directors should change it into very clear and common words.

The Scenery of Guilin 195

Reality is never as flawless as the illusory realm of ideals. I think anyone with a little experience would agree with this! This is not just my own old-fashioned opinion.

No matter how much scholars and men of letters use their flowery writing or eloquent tongues to promote the scenery of some places as being wonderfully like a fairyland, or to describe them as a peach blossom paradise, there is always the regret that "the reality is difficult to match the reputation." Therefore, when people mention "Guilin" and immediately have the illusion of "the best scenery in the world," I deeply feel disappointed for them!

Of course, Guilin has its own unique beauty; however, it is a beauty of stillness, and its era has long become a historical relic. Because it is still a medieval city, the people who live there, no matter what their occupations are, always appear leisurely and relaxed, unhurried in our eyes. There is no need to doubt that the world-famous scenery surrounding Guilin City is certainly as still as an ancient painting. No matter how much these landscapes are full of "natural beauty," as long as people are used to urban life, or even tired of urban life, they will inevitably have a sense of detachment! And the scenery of Guilin can all be painted; but as long as you live there for ten days or half a month, you will gradually feel that you are in the desert, and you will inevitably hum, "If this goes on, will I die of thirst?" So the scenery also has a sense of era!

So, what is the scenery of Guilin after all?

Let's talk about the mountains first!

The mountains in the Guilin area are mostly rocky and craggy, with towering cliffs and strange peaks, looking like they are artificially built. Although the mountains are bare, the color is actually verdant. There is Duxiu Peak in the city, behind the old imperial city. The mountain is more than ten feet high. Climbing up the steps, the city and fields are clearly visible. It is a pity that the pollution is very serious, and excrement and urine are all over the top of the mountain, so Duxiu Peak has turned into a unique stink. Guishan Mountain in the north of the city is also known as Fengdong Mountain. The mountain has a stone cave that runs through east and west. The cold wind is blowing. Even if you pass through this during the dog days of summer, you will feel that all the stuffiness has disappeared. Crossing the river, there are scenic spots such as Putuo Mountain, Crescent Mountain, and Seven Star Cave. The mountains all have caves, and the greatest is Seven Star Cave. The cave is very deep, and you cannot walk during the day without lighting a candle. The rocks in the cave are protruding, the spring water is dripping, and the atmosphere is gloomy and cold, with a ghostly aura; the cave is more than two miles long, running through north and south. However, there is a cave that is said to reach Hengyang, Hunan. Although this is the nonsense of those guides, it shows the depth of this cave. There is Elephant Trunk Hill in the south of the city, on the bank of the Li River, and the shape is very similar, especially its nose. In short, the mountains of Guilin are almost all volcanic rock mountains. The mountains must have caves, and they constitute various landscapes. In my opinion, they are unique, but there is absolutely no sense of greatness.

Secondly, let's talk about the water of Guilin.

The Guijiang River, also known as the Li River, surrounds the north, east, south, and east of the city. The water is shallow and there are many shoals, and there are many fine stones in the river. The water is clear and you can see the bottom. If you lean on the shore to fish, you can count the fish. The water is clear, but it does not surpass the water of all the source areas.

Because I stayed in Guilin for a slightly longer period of time, the beauty I felt for the so-called "world-famous" "landscape" was only like this. Other than that, I dare not promote it and make the general public who have not experienced it look forward to it with wide eyes. July 26th.

Night Talk 196

— Lin Xi

Let us revisit the poems of the Tang Dynasty,

You are silent,

I am also silent.

Silently, you don't inquire about my news,

I don't inquire about yours either;

We only warm: What evening is this?

What evening is this?

I have no leeks, no spring chives, no wine,

What I have is a wrinkled face, like yours.

Like yours, can you also tell you some news?

This reminds me

Of the footprints on the beach sand.

Guiying's Father (8) 199

— Ye Zi

"When the news of Xiaoyu's execution came, I was already so ill that I didn't know anything. After I recovered and learned the news, it didn't hurt so much. I believe this was the retribution for my previous arrest of the revolutionaries. It's just that my alcohol capacity suddenly dropped from six bowls to two, my strength has also declined, and my appearance has aged. My temperament has also become confused. Sometimes I don't have any feelings in my heart, but I just want to cry inexplicably. Sometimes I remember the past completely, and I want to tell everyone I meet. Sometimes I meet Master Zhuang Si on the street, and I also grab him and tell him my story, and when I tell him about when he came to my house and bowed to me and called me Old Master, his face often turns red. Haha, Master Zhuang Si once called me Lai Tou San the Old Master!"

Speaking of this, he stopped, drank the half bowl of wine in his hand, picked up a peanut and chewed it for a while.

"Mr. Xu, it's sad to talk about such things, but I can't help but talk about it. It's more sad if I don't talk about it. Xiaoyu has been dead for more than six years, and I have told this story hundreds of times. I feel like it's not me who wants to tell this story, it's like Xiaoyu wants me to tell it. I remember everything Xiaoyu said when he was alive, and I believe it all. He told me to let his mother, and I obeyed him. I can also tell all the principles he said about the poor and the rich. Every market day, I sit under the city gate selling sweet potato vermicelli, and I tell these principles to the villagers, and they all love to listen, and they all say that my Xiaoyu is a good person. In this way, my sweet potato vermicelli business has also improved."

When the four or five peanuts were also finished, he took out twelve copper coins from his pocket and spread them one by one on the counter.

"A Ren, take the money! Goodbye, Mr. Xu. It's getting late, and I have to cook for my wife. This wife, she should be killed, she should be killed, but I see Xiaoyu's face."

He staggered to the street. Seeing a dog, he shouted loudly, grabbed the dog's hind legs, and threw it more than ten feet away. The people watching laughed again, and then dispersed.

— Gou Fo

Nothing to talk about, talk about celebrity calligraphy and paintings, doing calligraphy and painting is already boring, talking about calligraphy and painting is even more boring,

Our country is a five-thousand-year-old civilized country, and antiques, calligraphy and paintings have their considerable value, which has long been recognized by all countries, and the so-called antiques are all from new to ancient, from ancient to more ancient, the times are inherited, and antiques, calligraphy and paintings are not replaced, if there are only old-fashioned antiques, and no new-brand antiques that follow, then antiques, calligraphy and paintings, will not be extinct in the world,

Return 219

— Dai Ni

After such good news came from the southern country in early summer, I waited every day for that accidental day to be today. Fei couldn't leave Shanghai, her second hometown, and she couldn't leave the Shanghai friends who needed her. But it made me have to think about the situation after we met, the triangle tragedy, we took great perseverance to escape from this vortex. Now that she has returned from Guangzhou after suffering all kinds of hardships, and after joining our group, I wonder what kind of situation will unfold again? She is a bold woman, or she will leave all the previous things in Guangzhou and start our new life: but women are women after all, her youth has run to the glorious end, even if she never wants to try that bitter cup of love again, a woman with no relatives, will she not think of her return? Can anyone in our group solve such a difficult problem for her? Guangzhou friends cannot comfort her, what will Shanghai friends use to comfort her? Coming to Shanghai still makes her feel greatly disappointed! Thinking of these times, I hope she will not return to Shanghai.

Since the beginning of summer, it has rained one day by chance 丨 This is really an accidental day. Jun's phone call came. He said that Fei had arrived in Shanghai. Because I moved, she couldn't find the place. She is now staying at the ×× Hotel, and asked me to go quickly after work. Although I hoped that she would not come to Shanghai again, I felt very happy when I heard the news. After leaving the office, I jumped into the rickshaw with an empty stomach and went to the designated place.

The car stopped at the neon lights. I remembered that we had separated here when we left. A slight sadness struck my heart. Take the elevator to the fifth floor

Page 22

, knocked on the room Jun told me, and the first one to rush out of the door was Fei, and I was the last one to arrive among the many friends who saw her off. For a moment, it seemed like I had broken into another happy world.

Fei hasn't changed. Except for her slightly darker complexion and being washed by the wind of the southern country, she grabbed my arm, as if guarding against me from escaping, and looked at my face playfully and said:

"Ah ×, did you eat spare rib sauce (meaning being scolded by your superiors)?" Before she finished speaking, she laughed loudly as if she couldn't breathe.

"Fei, I'm sick!" I deliberately lowered my voice and coughed.

"Really?" She turned her head and swept her eyes across everyone's faces, but everyone pretended to be serious. She pulled me to sit on the sofa, patted my shoulder,

"Ah ×, you have worked too hard!" She couldn't continue talking, and leaned her head on the back of the sofa.

An unexpected burst of laughter made her raise her head in surprise. She saw me smiling slightly too, and hurriedly wiped her eyes, pushed me angrily and jumped up, took out a cigarette from the stage and smoked alone, staring at the smoke rings as if she didn't want to pay attention to anyone.

I dragged her out and said, "Fei, what's the matter? Don't you want to see us?" I said to everyone at the same time. "We should live happily. Our Fei has returned. Let's watch Fishing Light Song tonight. It's more interesting than drinking brandy in a ballroom!" "Is it more interesting than drinking brandy in a ballroom?" I repeated, grabbing her shoulders. Fei finally smiled, turned around and escaped my grasp, threw the cigarette butt out the window, grabbed her silver bell purse, and said, holding it high, "I'm paying!"

"Welcome, Jewish millionaire!" Two hands raised from the corner.

The Donkey and Its Owner 220

— Wenli

Since moving into the new house, the first deep impression I had was of the horses rented out for people to ride, tied to the bamboo fence on the wasteland at the roadside near the alley entrance. Among them, there was a female donkey mixed in with the horses, always wailing mournfully every day. The sound of its wailing made one's nerves tremble. This sound also reminded me of my life in × place the year before. There, four donkeys were used in the public kitchen to drag the millstone to grind wheat. When they were released to rest, they were tied under the willow trees and exposed to the sun until they could barely breathe, so they competed to wail at each other. I was most afraid of hearing their wailing there. Sometimes, when there was no way to avoid it, I had to cover my ears with both hands. But no matter how much you covered your ears, their wailing would always drill in and knock against your eardrums, making you feel very uncomfortable. Now, walking past the roadside every day, I was unavoidably disturbed by the donkey's wailing, which made me feel a sour and sad emotion in my heart. And this sadness was not caused by any specific object that made me feel sad, but simply because hearing its voice made me feel uncomfortable.

The donkey was a black donkey with a large patch of white hair on its back. Perhaps because it had suffered too much hardship and not eaten or drunk enough, it was so thin that you could only see its bones, and its eyes were dull and lifeless, with white fluid flowing from them. It was an old, sick donkey. Although the horses beside it were not particularly strong or magnificent, it was still a frail, sick donkey. In comparison, how aged and insignificant it was! No wonder it wailed, I thought to myself.

The donkey's owner, on the other hand, was a hunchbacked, short old man! Whenever he saw pedestrians passing by his side stopping to look at his donkey, he would always offer a smiling face, bow, and lean his body at a sixty-degree angle to people, saying, "Ride donkey, want to? Ride donkey, want to?" But he was often met with cold eyes, and people would silently walk on their way. Once, I was attracted by the donkey's wailing and wanted to see why it was crying so miserably. As I stopped and carefully looked at it, the old man shouted at me in a miserable voice, catching me off guard, "Ride donkey, want to?" I shifted my attention away from the donkey and turned to look at its owner. Beneath his grey hair was a withered, tired, and sallow face, with grey eyebrows, a grey beard, and grey eyes. Wrinkles etched the traces of a lifetime of hard work and sorrow on his forehead and the corners of his mouth. His expressionless, blank look, and the way he spoke as if he wanted to laugh and cry at the same time, resonated with sympathy in my heart. The iron whip of life had bent his back and turned his hair and beard grey, yet he was still struggling for survival.

A child wearing a primary school uniform, about eight or nine years old, was pestering his father, a gentleman in a Western suit, to ride a horse. The old man, with a smiling face – still that same expression as if he wanted to laugh and cry – said to him, "Ride donkey, want to?" His father said, "Riding a horse is too dangerous." But the child insisted on riding a horse, looking down on the donkey, saying, "It's too dirty and small, I don't want it." His father said, "The horse is too dangerous, you can't ride it, you'll fall and die." The child started to cry, "The donkey doesn't run fast, I don't want it." His father laughed loudly, "Doesn't run fast, don't want it!" The child said, "The horse runs fast, I'm not afraid – isn't that person leading it in front?" For the father to have him ride a donkey was simply the best opportunity for the old man. He quickly flattered, saying, "My donkey can run fast, faster than a horse!" Faster than a horse – this was only a way to coax a child. The gentleman laughed loudly again when he heard it, laughing at him for lying. But the child also refused to be fooled, saying fiercely to the old man, "Don't I know? Horses are faster than donkeys! Daddy, I want to ride a horse." Not knowing whether the gentleman thought the old man was not being honest, or whether he cherished his son, he listened to the child and was dragged to a large horse. The old man was disappointed, but his expression didn't show it. He asked passers-by again, "Ride donkey, want to?" He was so used to people's indifference that no cold stimulation could move his numb heart.

Every time I walked past there, I always heard the donkey's wailing, which made my nerves tremble, and at the same time, I saw the old man saying to passers-by, "Ride donkey, want to?" But I never saw anyone riding his donkey. The cold indifference could not stir the old man's heart, but it touched my sensitive heart.

Starting from the Crow's Caw 221

— Shuihua

Waking up very early, the cool breeze and light mist were ruling the world. Breathing in the cool air flowing in from the window and watching the green paulownia leaves sway in the light mist, everything was quiet before me, and my heart was hazy. Somewhere hidden, little birds were chirping, and somewhere hidden, frogs were croaking. The green grassland was stretched out, lying down.

"Quah, quah, quah, quah," suddenly several black shadows cut through the grey sky and rushed past. A series of "quah, quah, quah, quah" sounds rained down. The black shadows had already flown far away, but the sounds had already stirred up ripples in my clear heart. Half of this was because the sound came so suddenly, and half, of course, was still the traditional subconscious effect – because this was the so-called ominous crow's caw.

The whirlpool of thought dispersed. I thought that believing that a crow's caw is ominous is of course a matter that has no room for discussion, but I felt that this superstition expresses people's selfishness to a certain extent.

Isn't this still selfishness? A crow's caw is just a crow's caw, but people don't acknowledge that it is the crow cawing itself. Instead, they want to say that the crow is cawing for some other purpose. Saying that the crow's caw has a purpose and not caring about it is one thing. The creatures that see and hear crows cawing in the sky are numerous to some extent, but people only say that their object is humans. Furthermore, there are so many people who see and hear crows cawing in the sky, but everyone feels that they are the object of the crows' caw. Why isn't the crow cawing itself but cawing for a purpose? Why isn't the object of the crow other creatures but humans? Why isn't the object of the crow someone else but myself? All of this can be said to be due only to people's selfishness with themselves as the subject.

Humans are truly a selfish thing. Not only is the idea of considering oneself the subject of everything in various superstitions selfish and ridiculous, but even in daily life, people are always showing how selfish they are. For example, suspicion breeds jealousy, resentment, and indignation. Which of these is not the result of selfishness? They all consider themselves the subject of everything, so they suspect others' actions,

Page 23

whether they look down on me; they are jealous of others' success because they believe that their skills are inferior to mine; they resent others' neglect because they believe that they have treated me wrongly; and they are indignant at others' failures because they believe that they intentionally insulted me. Extending this to everything, the truly arrogant, tyrannical, and even everything dictatorial does not arise from the selfishness of considering oneself remarkable. Truly, all kinds of troubles arise from this, and all kinds of sins are accomplished by this.

People are truly a pitiful group of creatures!

The Boss's Face 222

— Ding

The boss's face is so scary. It's always so angry, so fierce, with no place to approach him or feel any goodwill. In short, his face is like that three hundred and sixty days a year. I have never seen him open his mouth to smile. I'm really afraid to see his face, unwilling to see his face, unhappy to see his face – if it were possible.

I often think: the boss had better get sick, and sick badly, always lying in bed – unable to move at all. That way, he wouldn't come to the store and put on his boss's face. That way, I could sit at the counter properly, secretly looking at Xue Rengui's expedition to the east, or glancing at the little girls passing by. Otherwise, I could chat with Ah Si. Wouldn't that be great!

But, heaven just has to go against me. Not only doesn't the boss get sick, but his body is incredibly strong, stronger than us young guys. Not one of us can compare with him. It's us who get sick instead. That's really painful. We still have to make a living. Where would we get the money to buy medicine? That makes things even more troublesome. The boss doesn't care if you live or die. You still have to do your job well. But how can a sick person do their job well? The boss doesn't treat you like a person. He doesn't care about you. He won't forgive you. He only cares about himself, only wants to save money and make money, oppress people, and exploit people. It's really bad luck to be a shop assistant.

I get scolded every day, and sometimes I even get slapped. I'm really furious. Am I not a person? You, the boss, are a person, but am I, Li Jin, not born of a mother? You're just a petty boss, a petty capitalist. What are you being so fierce for? What are you being so imposing for? I'll see if you can be imposing to the end! I'm really not convinced by my boss's attitude.

But what's the point of not being convinced? What can I do to him? He has all the money, he's the boss, and I'm the shop assistant. So, I have to put up with his attitude. If I were the boss, I would be like that too. I would put on the boss's face. If he were my shop assistant, he would have to be at my command, listen to my orders, or else, I would tell him to get out! I would be fierce too. In short, being a boss is like that. There's nothing good to say about it. Because the boss is the boss and the shop assistant is the shop assistant. There's a river separating us.

Thinking about things like this, I really think it's not right, not right at all. Why does it have to be like that? Can't it be different? – The boss doesn't oppress us, and we don't resist the boss! We all make a living peacefully. Wouldn't that be good for everyone?

But, it can't be like that! Because the world isn't like that. If there are rich people, there will naturally be poor ghosts. If there are bosses, there will naturally be shop assistants. Everyone has a different status. So, I think we will never get along with the boss, and the boss doesn't bother to get along with us either. He has all the money, what's he afraid of? But, if we don't have work, we'll starve to death! We rely on the boss to live!

The Landlady 223

— Ruowang

The landlady is sick, no, she has a little treasure in her belly, doesn't want to eat, but wants to eat sour things, the cries of hawkers selling sugared plums make her excited, and Chen Yumei's lullaby makes her think of the taste of being a mother.

Her husband has a job and is not at home during the day. The landlady is alone in the room, comfortably lying on the bed. Chen Yumei's lullaby lulls the landlady to sleep.

Occasionally, the landlady issues one or two commands from the bed –

"Old man, watch the door." – The old man is her grandfather.

"Grand Uncle, hurry up and cook, my belly is hungry."

"Sister, wash my pants for me."

The Grand Uncle seems very apologetic, smiling as he walks to the door of the landlady's room, asking this female commander, female emperor what dishes she wants to eat. The female commander usually doesn't speak much, but when she does, it must be done. We can also understand that the money is in the landlady's hands, so nothing is impossible. But the Grand Uncle has no money. Without money, he can only swallow his pride and listen to the landlady's orders, so the Grand Uncle becomes a nephew instead.

In the evening, the sound of the husband's footsteps is outside the door. The landlady immediately closes her eyes tightly, pretending to be fast asleep, waiting for her husband to walk into the room and rest for a while before she wakes up from her dream. She scolds her husband in a spoiled voice for coming back so late.

The husband is Americanized, taking out the fruit hidden in the drawer and peeling it for the landlady to eat.

The old man is watching the door, the Grand Uncle is busy in the kitchen until his face is flushed, the husband is busy peeling fruit, and the landlady is busy acting spoiled. And so the sky gradually darkens.

"It's getting hot, cut some ×× gauze for me tomorrow to make clothes, don't forget." This command is issued to the husband, and we can imagine that the husband will certainly obey.

But the husband also has his own hardships. Although it is rare for him to have no money, there are always unfortunate times.

The next evening, the sound of the husband's footsteps is again outside the door. The landlady closes her eyes tightly, pretending not to know. As usual, the husband doesn't dare to make a noise, quietly walking around the room, seeming a little uneasy.

"Why did you come back so late today?"

The husband is peeling the skin of the fruit.

"Where's the fabric?"

The husband stuffs a mandarin orange into her mouth, but it is slapped away by the landlady, who turns her body around, facing inward. Ugh! Ugh! She's going to vomit, huh! huh! She really seems sick.

The husband sits on the bed and pats her back, very patiently, without saying a word. The landlady wriggles her body, not wanting him to pat her. If he pats her, it's not right, if he doesn't pat her, it's not right. There's really no way.

The old man's belly is growling with hunger. The Grand Uncle often walks to the door of the room and looks in. A table full of food has gone cold, but he doesn't dare to ask. And the landlady's illness is becoming increasingly serious. The stalemate continues indefinitely.

The old man is secretly eating fatty meat. The Grand Uncle is like a wooden puppet, without any ideas. But the landlady is leaning in her husband's arms. But how will this awkward situation end? The husband has to tell her his secret, and unexpectedly gains the landlady's favor.

"Why didn't you say so earlier? If you don't have money, I have it here. You didn't even know how to tell the color of the fabric. Come on, let's go buy it together." The landlady's fussiness seems to have disappeared. Yes, she didn't really have any illness.

Finally, the landlady went out with her husband.

On the way back, the landlady has a package of fabric in her hand and whispers in her husband's ear in a sparsely populated place, "Let's stay outside tonight, just like when we weren't married." The husband agreed, but the old man is guarding the door, still sitting there late into the night.

The Problem of Housing 224

— Weifeng

Clothing, food, and housing are the three major problems. In Shanghai, housing is the most difficult to solve. A salaried employee often has a large portion of their income taken up by housing. And within a room that is less than a few square feet, the bedroom, kitchen, and toilet are all squeezed in, calling it a pigeon coop, which is very appropriate. If a person without permanent assets suddenly loses their job, it is truly unimaginable! Shanghai is a place where every inch of land is worth gold. Half of this is due to the manipulation of real estate brokers, and half is due to the large number of people crowding into the city after bankruptcy in the countryside. As a result, places that were once deserted are now tall buildings and mansions. The increasing prosperity of the city also means the increasing exploitation of the petty bourgeoisie.

A salaried employee sometimes has to consider the distance to their workplace and the cost of transportation. Their home often has to be moved frequently due to their job. As a result, the difficulty of moving is constantly on their mind.

Shanghai is originally a den of all kinds of evils. Previous incidents have frightened the landlords, so there are regulations such as "No inquiries without family, no rent without guarantor." When I came to Shanghai as a bachelor, although I was fortunate enough not to be unemployed, I encountered great difficulties in renting a house. In the bustling areas closer to my workplace, even a small attic room often cost more than ten yuan, and there were unexpected problems such as midnight lights and all-night lights, and quarrels with the landlords. Moreover, in a Shikumen house, there were all kinds of people, sometimes making it difficult to sleep at night, and thefts also occurred from time to time. If I rented a house in an area farther from my workplace, the cost of transportation often accumulated into an alarming amount in a month, and various difficulties might arise in terms of time.

Later, my salary was higher, but after a bachelor became a cohabiting couple, the housing situation could no longer be the same as when I was single. Although an attic room could still accommodate me, the visits of my wife's family made it necessary to expand your living space. And as your professional status slightly increased, you also had more friends. As a result, friendship and professional relationships also made it necessary to expand your living space when friends came to visit you. Although the bedroom could also serve as a kitchen and toilet, a woman often did not have the same convenience as a man. If it also served as a reception room, various unexpected

difficulties would arise.

This is still the case for a small family. If you are responsible for the heavy burden of a large family, your parents, siblings, and children, even if they are your own family, cannot but add a few more pigeon coops. A salaried employee does not know how to allocate their expenses.

This is the development of a distorted society: on the one hand, large hotels and inns are increasing day by day, and on the other hand, people who have only had thin porridge are worrying about not being able to find a place to shelter from the wind and rain. However, on the surface, it is naturally obscured by prosperity. Many oppressed classes can only swallow their anger and remain silent.
